## **13. Control Volume and Control Mass**

|------|--------------|

## **14. Real vs Ideal Systems**

- **Ideal Gas:** Obeys PV = RT perfectly.  
- **Real Gas:** Deviates from ideal at high pressure / low temperature.

# ğŸ”¥ Chapter 2 â€“ First Law of Thermodynamics

## **Overview**

First Law of Thermodynamics á€€á€­á€¯ â€œLaw of Conservation of Energyâ€ á€œá€­á€¯á€·á€œá€Šá€ºá€¸á€á€±á€«á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  
á€¡á€“á€­á€€á€á€˜á€±á€¬á€á€›á€¬á€¸á€€á€á€±á€¬á€· â€”
> **Energy cannot be created or destroyed; it can only be transformed from one form to another.**

á€†á€­á€¯á€á€²á€· á€¡á€šá€°á€¡á€†á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Heat, Work, Internal Energy, Enthalpy á€…á€á€²á€· Energy Forms á€á€½á€±á€€á€­á€¯ á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€á€•á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

## **1. Energy Conservation Principle**

System á€‘á€²á€€á€­á€¯ á€‘á€Šá€·á€ºá€á€²á€· Heat Energy (Q)  
á€”á€²á€· System á€™á€¾ á€‘á€½á€€á€ºá€á€½á€¬á€¸á€á€²á€· Work (W) á€¡á€€á€¼á€¬á€¸ á€†á€€á€ºá€”á€½á€šá€ºá€™á€¾á€¯á€€ á€¡á€“á€­á€€á€•á€«á‹

**Mathematical form:**


Q - W = Î”E

Where Î”E = Change in total energy of the system  
= Î”U (Internal Energy) + Î”KE (Kinetic Energy) + Î”PE (Potential Energy)

---

## **2. Closed System (Control Mass)**

Closed System á€™á€¾á€¬ Mass á€™á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€•á€«á‹  
Energy (Heat, Work) á€á€­á€¯á€·á€€á€á€±á€¬á€· á€á€½á€¬á€¸á€œá€¬á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

**Energy Balance Equation:**


Q - W = Î”U + Î”KE + Î”PE


If KE, PE changes are small â†’  


Q - W = Î”U


á€’á€«á€€ â€œInternal Energyâ€ á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€™á€¾á€¯á€€á€­á€¯ á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€á€•á€ºá€á€²á€·á€¡á€á€”á€ºá€¸á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

## **3. Sign Conventions**

| Direction | Heat (Q) | Work (W) |
|------------|-----------|-----------|
| Into System | Positive (+) | Negative (-) |
| Out of System | Negative (-) | Positive (+) |

á€‰á€•á€™á€¬ â€“  
- Gas compressed â†’ Work done **on** the system (W negative).  
- Gas expands â†’ Work done **by** the system (W positive).  

---

## **4. Work Done in Various Processes**

**(a) Boundary Work (PdV Work)**  
System volume á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€™á€¾á€¯á€›á€¾á€­á€á€²á€·á€¡á€á€« á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  


W = âˆ« P dV


**(b) Constant Pressure Process (Isobaric)**  


W = P (Vâ‚‚ - Vâ‚)


**(c) Polytropic Process (PVâ¿ = C)**  


W = (Pâ‚‚Vâ‚‚ - Pâ‚Vâ‚) / (1 - n)

For n = 1 â†’ Isothermal Process â†’ W = Pâ‚Vâ‚ ln(Vâ‚‚/Vâ‚)

## **5. Internal Energy (U)**

Internal Energy á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€™á€±á€¬á€ºá€œá€®á€€á€»á€°á€¸á€¡á€†á€„á€·á€ºá€™á€¾á€¬á€›á€¾á€­á€á€²á€·  
Microscopic Energy (Translation, Rotation, Vibration) á€á€½á€±á€•á€«á€á€„á€ºá€á€²á€· Energy á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  

For **Ideal Gas**:


U = f(T)

â‡’ Internal Energy is a function of Temperature only.

**Change in Internal Energy:**


Î”U = m Ã— c_v Ã— (Tâ‚‚ - Tâ‚)


---

## **6. Enthalpy (H)**

**Definition:**


H = U + PÂ·V


**Change in Enthalpy:**


Î”H = Î”U + Î”(PV)


For Ideal Gas â†’ PV = RT  


Î”H = m Ã— c_p Ã— (Tâ‚‚ - Tâ‚)


Enthalpy á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ Constant Pressure Process á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€¡á€á€½á€€á€º á€¡á€›á€±á€¸á€€á€¼á€®á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

## **7. Open System (Control Volume)**

Open System á€™á€¾á€¬ Mass á€á€½á€¬á€¸á€œá€¬á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  
Turbine, Compressor, Nozzle, Heat Exchanger á€…á€á€²á€· Devices á€á€½á€±á€™á€¾á€¬ á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

**Steady Flow Energy Equation (SFEE):**


(QÌ‡ - WÌ‡) = á¹ [ (hâ‚‚ - hâ‚) + Â½ (Vâ‚‚Â² - Vâ‚Â²) + g (zâ‚‚ - zâ‚) ]


Where â€“  
- h = Enthalpy (U + PV)  
- V = Velocity  
- z = Elevation  
- á¹ = Mass Flow Rate  

---

## **8. Application Examples**

### **(a) Nozzle**
Work = 0, Potential Energy negligible  


hâ‚ + Vâ‚Â²/2 = hâ‚‚ + Vâ‚‚Â²/2

â‡’ Enthalpy drop = Kinetic energy gain  

---

### **(b) Compressor or Pump**
Work input required â†’  


WÌ‡ = á¹ (hâ‚‚ - hâ‚)


---

### **(c) Turbine**
Work output â†’  


WÌ‡ = á¹ (hâ‚ - hâ‚‚)


---

### **(d) Heat Exchanger**
No Work exchange (W = 0)  


QÌ‡ = á¹ (hâ‚‚ - hâ‚)


---

## **9. Per Unit Mass Form**

For ease of analysis:


q - w = Î”u + Î”ke + Î”pe

where q = Q/m , w = W/m

## **11. Limitations of the First Law**

# â™»ï¸ Chapter 3 â€“ Second Law of Thermodynamics

---

## **Overview**

First Law of Thermodynamics á€€ Energy á€›á€²á€· Conservation á€€á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€á€á€ºá€™á€¾á€á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

Second Law á€€á€á€±á€¬á€·  
> **Energy Transformation á€™á€¾á€¬ Directionality (á€¡á€”á€Šá€ºá€¸á€†á€¯á€¶á€¸á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€²á€· á€¦á€¸á€á€Šá€ºá€á€»á€€á€º)** á€€á€­á€¯ á€á€á€ºá€™á€¾á€á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹  

á€¡á€á€­á€¯á€á€»á€¯á€¶á€¸ â€”  
**"First Law = Quantity of Energy"**,  
**"Second Law = Quality of Energy."**

## **1. Limitations of the First Law**

First Law á€Ÿá€¬  
> â€œQ - W = Î”Uâ€  
á€†á€­á€¯á€•á€¼á€®á€¸ Energy Conservation á€€á€­á€¯á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€•á€±á€™á€²á€·  
á€’á€«á€€á€á€±á€¬á€· â€” Heat â†’ Work á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€•á€±á€™á€²á€·, Work â†’ Heat á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€›á€¬á€á€½á€„á€º áá€á€% á€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€™á€›á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€¬á€€á€­á€¯ á€™á€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€•á€«á‹  

á€¡á€²á€’á€®á€¡á€›á€¬á€€á€­á€¯á€á€±á€¬á€· Second Law á€–á€¼á€„á€·á€º á€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€œá€Šá€ºá€á€á€ºá€™á€¾á€á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

## **2. Kelvinâ€“Planck Statement**

> â€œIt is impossible for any cyclic device to convert all the heat received from a single heat reservoir completely into work.â€

á€á€­á€¯á€·á€†á€­á€¯á€›á€„á€º â€”  
**No heat engine can be 100% efficient.**

Heat Engine á€á€…á€ºá€œá€¯á€¶á€¸á€Ÿá€¬ Heat Source (High Temperature Reservoir) á€™á€¾ á€¡á€…á€½á€™á€ºá€¸á€¡á€‘á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€šá€°á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Heat Sink (Low Temperature Reservoir) á€á€­á€¯á€· á€¡á€á€»á€­á€¯á€·á€€á€­á€¯ á€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€‘á€¯á€á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€›á€á€šá€ºá‹



Qâ‚ â†’ Engine â†’ W + Qâ‚‚


**Efficiency (Î·):**


Î· = W / Qâ‚ = 1 - (Qâ‚‚ / Qâ‚)


---

## **3. Clausius Statement**

> â€œIt is impossible to construct a device which operates in a cycle and transfers heat from a colder body to a hotter body without any external work.â€

á€’á€«á€†á€­á€¯á€á€±á€¬á€· Refrigeration Process á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€–á€­á€¯á€·  
**External Work** á€œá€­á€¯á€¡á€•á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  
â†’ á€¡á€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€„á€”á€ºá€¸á€™á€¾á€¬ á€¡á€„á€ºá€¡á€¬á€¸á€‘á€Šá€·á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€›á€á€šá€ºá‹

## **4. Heat Engine and Heat Pump**

| Device | Function | Heat Flow | Work Direction |
|---------|-----------|------------|----------------|
| **Heat Engine** | Converts heat â†’ work | High â†’ Low | Output |
| **Refrigerator** | Maintains low temperature | Low â†’ High | Input |
| **Heat Pump** | Transfers heat to warm space | Low â†’ High | Input |

**COP (Coefficient of Performance):**

- Refrigerator â†’ `COP_R = Q_L / W`
- Heat Pump â†’ `COP_HP = Q_H / W = COP_R + 1`

---

## **5. Reversible and Irreversible Processes**

**Reversible Process**  
â†’ Ideal process, no losses, system returns to original state without any effect on surroundings.

**Irreversible Process**  
â†’ Real process, friction, heat loss, unbalanced forces present.

### **Causes of Irreversibility**
- Friction & Viscous Effects  
- Unrestrained Expansion  
- Heat Transfer with Finite Temperature Difference  
- Mixing of Different Substances  

---

## **6. Carnot Cycle**

Nicolas LÃ©onard Sadi Carnot á€á€Šá€º  
**Perfect (Reversible) Heat Engine** á€€á€­á€¯ á€•á€‘á€™á€†á€¯á€¶á€¸ á€¡á€…á€‰á€ºá€¡á€œá€¬á€”á€²á€· á€á€á€ºá€™á€¾á€á€ºá€á€²á€·á€á€šá€ºá‹

### **Processes of Carnot Cycle**
1. **Isothermal Expansion (1â€“2)** â†’ Heat absorbed (Qâ‚)  
2. **Adiabatic Expansion (2â€“3)** â†’ Temperature drops  
3. **Isothermal Compression (3â€“4)** â†’ Heat rejected (Qâ‚‚)  
4. **Adiabatic Compression (4â€“1)** â†’ Temperature rises  

**Efficiency:**


Î·_Carnot = 1 - (Tâ‚‚ / Tâ‚)

(Temperature in Kelvin)

**Key Point:**  
Carnot Efficiency á€á€Šá€º Temperature Ratio á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€¡á€•á€±á€«á€ºá€á€¬ á€™á€°á€á€Šá€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Working Substance á€™á€°á€á€Šá€ºá€™á€¾á€¯ á€™á€›á€¾á€­á€•á€«á‹

## **7. Reversible Refrigerator / Heat Pump (Carnot Type)**

**COP (Carnot Refrigerator):**


COP_R = T_L / (T_H - T_L)


**COP (Carnot Heat Pump):**


COP_HP = T_H / (T_H - T_L)


á€’á€®á€¡á€á€»á€­á€¯á€·á€€ á€¡á€™á€¼á€„á€·á€ºá€†á€¯á€¶á€¸ theoretical performance á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
á€¡á€™á€¾á€”á€ºá€á€€á€šá€ºá€™á€¾á€¬ Efficiency / COP á€”á€Šá€ºá€¸á€œá€¬á€á€á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

# â™¾ï¸ Chapter 4 â€“ Entropy and Clausius Inequality

## **Overview**

## **1. Clausius Inequality**

Clausius á€€ 1850s á€™á€¾á€¬ á€á€€á€ºá€†á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€›á€¬ Integral Relationship á€€á€­á€¯ á€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€á€²á€·á€á€šá€ºá‹

**Mathematical Form:**


âˆ® (Î´Q / T) â‰¤ 0


- For **Reversible Cycle:** `âˆ® (Î´Q_rev / T) = 0`  
- For **Irreversible Cycle:** `âˆ® (Î´Q_irrev / T) < 0`

á€’á€®á€¡á€á€»á€€á€ºá€€á€á€±á€¬á€· Second Law á€€á€­á€¯ á€á€€á€ºá€†á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€¡á€±á€¬á€„á€º á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€²á€· á€•á€¯á€¶á€…á€¶á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

## **2. Entropy Definition**

á€’á€«á€†á€­á€¯á€›á€„á€º Reversible Path á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€…á€±áŠ Irreversible Path á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€…á€±

**Cycle á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€¡á€á€½á€€á€º:**


âˆ® dS = 0


á€¡á€²á€·á€’á€«á€€ Entropy á€Ÿá€¬ Property á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€á€€á€ºá€á€±á€¡á€‘á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

## **4. Entropy Change of System and Surroundings**

System á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯ Process á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€²á€·á€¡á€á€«  
Entropy Change á€”á€¾á€…á€ºá€™á€»á€­á€¯á€¸á€›á€¾á€­á€á€šá€ºá‹



Î”S_universe = Î”S_system + Î”S_surroundings


- For **Reversible Process:** Î”S_universe = 0  
- For **Irreversible Process:** Î”S_universe > 0  

> Entropy of the Universe never decreases.

## **5. Entropy Change for Common Processes**

### **(a) Isothermal Process (Ideal Gas)**


Î”S = mÂ·RÂ·ln(Vâ‚‚/Vâ‚) = mÂ·RÂ·ln(Pâ‚/Pâ‚‚)

Î”S = mÂ·c_vÂ·ln(Tâ‚‚/Tâ‚)


### **(d) Phase Change (Melting, Vaporization)**

## **6. Entropy Change for Ideal Gas (General Form)**

For Ideal Gas:

## **7. Tâ€“S Diagram (Temperatureâ€“Entropy Diagram)**

Tâ€“S Diagram á€€á€­á€¯ Thermodynamic Process á€á€½á€± á€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€–á€­á€¯á€· á€¡á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

| Process | Representation on Tâ€“S Diagram |
|----------|-------------------------------|
| Isothermal | Horizontal Line |
| Adiabatic | Vertical Line |
| Isobaric | Curved Line |
| Isochoric | Inclined Line |

**Area under Tâ€“S Curve = Heat Transfer (Q_rev).**

---

## **8. Entropy Generation (S_gen)**

Irreversible Process á€á€½á€„á€º Entropy á€•á€­á€¯á€™á€­á€¯á€á€­á€¯á€¸á€á€á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

**Entropy Balance Equation:**


Î”S_system = âˆ«(Î´Q / T_boundary) + S_gen


Where S_gen â‰¥ 0  
- Reversible â†’ S_gen = 0  
- Irreversible â†’ S_gen > 0  

Entropy Generation á€á€Šá€º Friction, Mixing, Heat Losses, etc.  
á€€á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€·á€º á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **9. Isolated System and the Universe**

For Isolated System â†’ No heat or mass transfer.  
Therefore,


Î”S_system = S_gen â‰¥ 0


That means â€”  
> In an isolated system, entropy always increases or remains constant.

á€’á€®á€¡á€€á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€Ÿá€¬ â€œNatural tendency towards equilibriumâ€ á€†á€­á€¯á€á€²á€· á€á€˜á€±á€¬á€á€›á€¬á€¸á€€á€­á€¯ á€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€á€šá€ºá‹

## **10. Physical Interpretation of Entropy**

Entropy á€Ÿá€¬ Thermal Energy á€›á€²á€· â€œAvailabilityâ€ á€€á€­á€¯ á€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€á€šá€ºá‹  
Energy á€á€Šá€º Quantity á€™á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€•á€±á€™á€²á€·  
**Quality** á€€á€á€±á€¬á€· Gradually Downward á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€½á€¬á€¸á€á€á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

Example:
- Reversible heat transfer â†’ No entropy generation  
- Irreversible heat transfer â†’ Increase in total entropy  

Entropy á€á€€á€ºá€œá€»á€¾á€„á€º System á€•á€­á€¯á€á€Šá€ºá€„á€¼á€­á€™á€ºá€œá€¬á€•á€¼á€®á€¸ Useful Work á€•á€¼á€¯á€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€…á€½á€™á€ºá€¸ á€œá€»á€±á€¬á€·á€€á€»á€á€šá€ºá‹

## **11. Entropy Change for the Universe (Total Entropy Concept)**

| Type of Process | Î”S_system | Î”S_surroundings | Î”S_total |
|------------------|-------------|--------------------|-----------|
| Reversible | +x | -x | 0 |
| Irreversible | +x | < -x | >0 |

> Nature always proceeds in the direction of increasing total entropy.

## **12. Entropy and Availability (Exergy)**

Availability (Exergy) á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ Useful Work Output á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€²á€· Potential á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

**Relationship:**

## **13. Principle of Increase of Entropy**

> For any real process, the total entropy of the system and its surroundings increases.

**Mathematically:**


Î”S_universe â‰¥ 0


Equality holds only for reversible processes.

---

## **14. Entropy in Isolated Systems**

- Reversible Process â†’ Entropy constant  
- Irreversible Process â†’ Entropy increases  
- Impossible Process â†’ Entropy decreases  

á€’á€«á€€á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€·á€º Nature á€™á€¾á€¬ á€á€˜á€¬á€á€¡á€á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€¸ á€œá€»á€¾á€±á€¬á€·á€™á€á€½á€¬á€¸á€˜á€²

## **Overview**

á€’á€®á€¡á€á€”á€ºá€¸á€™á€¾á€¬á€á€±á€¬á€· Thermodynamic State Functions (U, H, A, G) á€á€½á€±á€¡á€€á€¼á€¬á€¸

á€’á€®á€¡á€á€”á€ºá€¸á€€ Engineering Thermodynamics á€›á€²á€· Analytical Core á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Entropy, Enthalpy, Internal Energy, Gibbs Function á€á€­á€¯á€·á€›á€²á€· Differential Form á€á€½á€±á€€á€­á€¯ á€†á€€á€ºá€á€½á€šá€ºá€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€á€šá€ºá‹

## **1. Thermodynamic Potentials**

Thermodynamic System á€€á€­á€¯ á€á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€¸á€á€¬á€›á€¬á€™á€¾á€¬ Energy Functions á€œá€±á€¸á€á€¯á€¡á€›á€±á€¸á€€á€¼á€®á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹  
á€’á€«á€á€½á€±á€€á€­á€¯ **Thermodynamic Potentials** á€œá€­á€¯á€·á€á€±á€«á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

| Symbol | Name | Definition | Natural Variables |
|---------|-------|-------------|--------------------|
| **U** | Internal Energy | U = Q - W | (S, V) |
| **H** | Enthalpy | H = U + PÂ·V | (S, P) |
| **A** | Helmholtz Free Energy | A = U - TÂ·S | (T, V) |
| **G** | Gibbs Free Energy | G = H - TÂ·S | (T, P) |

---

## **2. Total Differential Forms**

State Function á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€¡á€á€½á€€á€º Total Differential á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ â€”
Property á€á€”á€ºá€–á€­á€¯á€¸á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€Ÿá€¬ á€¡á€á€¼á€¬á€¸ Variables á€”á€¾á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€¡á€•á€±á€«á€º á€™á€°á€á€Šá€ºá€™á€¾á€¯á€€á€­á€¯ á€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€á€šá€ºá‹

**Example:**


dU = (âˆ‚U/âˆ‚S)_V Â· dS + (âˆ‚U/âˆ‚V)_S Â· dV


Thermodynamics á€™á€¾á€¬ â€”


dU = TÂ·dS - PÂ·dV

á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€¬á€€á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€·á€º  


(âˆ‚U/âˆ‚S)_V = T
(âˆ‚U/âˆ‚V)_S = -P


á€’á€®á€œá€­á€¯ Differential Equations á€á€½á€±á€€ Maxwell Relations á€á€Šá€ºá€†á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€›á€¬ á€¡á€á€¼á€±á€á€¶á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

## **3. Exact Differential Condition**

Function á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯ f(x, y) á€Ÿá€¬ Exact Differential á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€–á€­á€¯á€·  
á€¡á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€•á€« Relationship á€œá€­á€¯á€¡á€•á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹



âˆ‚Â²f/âˆ‚xâˆ‚y = âˆ‚Â²f/âˆ‚yâˆ‚x


Thermodynamics á€™á€¾á€¬á€á€±á€¬á€·


(âˆ‚/âˆ‚V)[(âˆ‚U/âˆ‚S)_V] = (âˆ‚/âˆ‚S)[(âˆ‚U/âˆ‚V)_S]


á€’á€«á€€ Maxwell Equations á€á€½á€±á€–á€½á€²á€·á€›á€¬á€¡á€á€½á€€á€º á€á€€á€ºá€†á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€•á€«á€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **4. Maxwell Relations**

Maxwell Relations á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬á€á€±á€¬á€·  
Four Thermodynamic Potentials á€á€½á€±á€€á€­á€¯ Partial Derivatives á€”á€²á€· á€†á€€á€ºá€…á€•á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€· Equations á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

### **(a) From Internal Energy (U):**


dU = TÂ·dS - PÂ·dV

â†’ Comparing coefficients â‡’  


(âˆ‚T/âˆ‚V)_S = - (âˆ‚P/âˆ‚S)_V


---

### **(b) From Enthalpy (H = U + PV):**


dH = TÂ·dS + VÂ·dP

â‡’  


(âˆ‚T/âˆ‚P)_S = (âˆ‚V/âˆ‚S)_P


---

### **(c) From Helmholtz Free Energy (A = U - TS):**


dA = -SÂ·dT - PÂ·dV

â‡’  


(âˆ‚S/âˆ‚V)_T = (âˆ‚P/âˆ‚T)_V


---

### **(d) From Gibbs Free Energy (G = H - TS):**


dG = -SÂ·dT + VÂ·dP

â‡’  


(âˆ‚S/âˆ‚P)_T = - (âˆ‚V/âˆ‚T)_P


---

ğŸ§© **Summary Table â€“ Maxwell Relations**

| Derived From | Differential Form | Maxwell Relation |
|---------------|------------------|------------------|
| **U(S,V)** | dU = TÂ·dS - PÂ·dV | (âˆ‚T/âˆ‚V)_S = - (âˆ‚P/âˆ‚S)_V |
| **H(S,P)** | dH = TÂ·dS + VÂ·dP | (âˆ‚T/âˆ‚P)_S = (âˆ‚V/âˆ‚S)_P |
| **A(T,V)** | dA = -SÂ·dT - PÂ·dV | (âˆ‚S/âˆ‚V)_T = (âˆ‚P/âˆ‚T)_V |
| **G(T,P)** | dG = -SÂ·dT + VÂ·dP | (âˆ‚S/âˆ‚P)_T = - (âˆ‚V/âˆ‚T)_P |

---

## **5. Significance of Maxwell Relations**

- Entropy á€€á€­á€¯ Measurement á€™á€œá€½á€šá€ºá€á€²á€· Variables (P, T, V) á€”á€²á€· á€†á€€á€ºá€…á€•á€ºá€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  
- Thermodynamic Data Analysis, Gas Equation Derivation, Real Substance Behavior á€á€½á€±á€™á€¾á€¬ á€¡á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹  
- Mathematical link between measurable quantities and inaccessible properties.

---

## **6. Specific Heat Relationships**

Specific Heats á€”á€²á€· Entropy Differential á€€á€­á€¯ á€†á€€á€ºá€á€½á€šá€ºá€œá€­á€¯á€·á€›á€á€šá€ºá‹



c_p - c_v = T (âˆ‚P/âˆ‚T)_V (âˆ‚V/âˆ‚T)_P


Ideal Gas á€¡á€á€½á€€á€º â†’  


c_p - c_v = R


á€’á€«á€€ Mayerâ€™s Relation á€œá€­á€¯á€·á€á€±á€«á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

## **7. Joule Coefficient (Î¼J)**

Joule Experiment á€™á€¾á€¬ Internal Energy (U) á€Ÿá€¬ Volume á€•á€±á€«á€º á€™á€°á€á€Šá€ºá€á€œá€¬á€¸ á€…á€™á€ºá€¸á€á€•á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹



Î¼_J = (âˆ‚T/âˆ‚V)_U


For Ideal Gas â†’ Î¼_J = 0  
(Internal Energy depends only on Temperature)

---

## **8. Jouleâ€“Thomson Effect**

Real Gases á€á€½á€„á€º Throttling Process á€™á€¾á€¬ Temperature á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€á€á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

**Coefficient:**


Î¼_JT = (âˆ‚T/âˆ‚P)_H


- Î¼_JT > 0 â†’ Cooling (e.g., COâ‚‚, Nâ‚‚)  
- Î¼_JT < 0 â†’ Heating (e.g., Hâ‚‚, He)

**Inversion Temperature (T_i):**
â†’ Temperature at which Î¼_JT = 0  

á€¡á€²á€’á€®á€”á€±á€›á€¬á€™á€¾á€¬ Throttling Effect á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **9. Energy Equations in Terms of Measurable Properties**

Using Maxwell Relations â†’  
Energy Differential á€€á€­á€¯ á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€¡á€”á€Šá€ºá€¸á€„á€šá€º á€á€»á€²á€·á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

**For Internal Energy:**


dU = c_vÂ·dT + [T(âˆ‚P/âˆ‚T)_V - P]Â·dV


**For Enthalpy:**


dH = c_pÂ·dT + [V - T(âˆ‚V/âˆ‚T)_P]Â·dP


á€’á€® Formulas á€á€½á€±á€€ Real Gas Data á€á€½á€±á€á€½á€€á€º á€¡á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **10. Combined Energy Equation**

Combining First & Second Laws â†’  


dU = TÂ·dS - PÂ·dV

From this, we can find expressions for **dH**, **dA**, and **dG**:

| Function | Expression | Differential Form |
|-----------|-------------|--------------------|
| **U** | Internal Energy | dU = TÂ·dS - PÂ·dV |
| **H** | Enthalpy | dH = TÂ·dS + VÂ·dP |
| **A** | Helmholtz Free Energy | dA = -SÂ·dT - PÂ·dV |
| **G** | Gibbs Free Energy | dG = -SÂ·dT + VÂ·dP |

---

## **11. Thermodynamic Property Relations**

Maxwell Relations á€€á€­á€¯ á€¡á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€•á€¼á€¯á€•á€¼á€®á€¸ Differential Properties á€á€½á€±á€€á€­á€¯  
Measurable Quantities á€”á€²á€· á€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

Examples:


(âˆ‚S/âˆ‚T)_P = c_p / T
(âˆ‚S/âˆ‚T)_V = c_v / T

## **13. Graphical Representation**

Tâ€“S, Pâ€“V, Hâ€“S (Mollier), and Gâ€“T Diagrams á€á€½á€±á€™á€¾á€¬  
Maxwell Relations á€€á€­á€¯ Curve Slope á€¡á€”á€±á€”á€²á€· á€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

Example:

â†’ Slope of isochoric line on Pâ€“T diagram = Slope of isothermal line on Sâ€“V diagram.

## **14. Summary of Core Relationships**

| Symbol | Definition | Main Use |
|----------|-------------|----------|
| U | Internal Energy | Fundamental Energy Function |
| H | Enthalpy | Flow Energy / Open Systems |
| A | Helmholtz Free Energy | Constant Volume, Isothermal Systems |
| G | Gibbs Free Energy | Constant Pressure, Isothermal Systems |

## **15. Key Engineering Implications**

- Real Gas Property Estimation, Refrigeration Analysis, Chemical Reaction Equilibrium á€á€½á€„á€º á€™á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€™á€”á€±á€œá€­á€¯á€¡á€•á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

## **á€¡á€”á€¾á€…á€ºá€á€»á€¯á€•á€º**

> Internal Energy, Enthalpy, Free Energies á€á€­á€¯á€·á€€á€­á€¯ á€†á€€á€ºá€á€½á€šá€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹  
> Engineering á€¡á€á€½á€€á€ºá€á€±á€¬á€· á€¡á€á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€¸á€¡á€á€¬á€™á€›á€¾á€­á€á€²á€· á€¡á€›á€±á€¸á€•á€«á€™á€¾á€¯á€›á€¾á€­á€á€šá€ºá‹

**á€¡á€€á€»á€‰á€ºá€¸á€á€»á€¯á€•á€º:**

> transforming abstract energy functions into practical equations of state.â€


á€¡á€á€¯ Chapter 5 á€¡á€•á€¼á€®á€¸á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€¬á€”á€²á€·

# ğŸ’§ Chapter 6 â€“ Pure Substances and Phase Change (Steam & Refrigerants)

## **Overview**

á€’á€®á€¡á€á€”á€ºá€¸á€™á€¾á€¬á€á€±á€¬á€· Pure Substances (á€á€”á€·á€ºá€›á€¾á€„á€ºá€¸á€á€±á€¬ á€•á€…á€¹á€…á€Šá€ºá€¸) á€á€½á€±á

á€”á€¾á€„á€·á€º Steam Tables, Refrigerants á€á€½á€±á€€á€­á€¯ á€œá€±á€·á€œá€¬á€™á€šá€ºá‹

Pure Substance á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€™á€±á€¬á€ºá€œá€®á€€á€»á€°á€¸á€á€…á€ºá€™á€»á€­á€¯á€¸á€á€­á€¯á€·á€™á€Ÿá€¯á€á€º Chemical Composition á€á€°á€Šá€®á€á€²á€·  
Substance á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹ á€¥á€•á€™á€¬ â€“ Water (Hâ‚‚O), COâ‚‚, Ammonia (NHâ‚ƒ), Refrigerants (R-22, R-134a) á€…á€á€²á€· á€¡á€›á€¬á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á‹

## **1. Definition of Pure Substance**

> **Pure Substance** á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ Homogeneous Chemical Composition á€á€°á€Šá€®á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
> Phase á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€™á€¾á€¯á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€…á€‰á€ºá€¡á€á€½á€„á€ºá€¸á€™á€¾á€¬á€•á€« Composition á€™á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€á€²á€· á€•á€…á€¹á€…á€Šá€ºá€¸ á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

á€¥á€•á€™á€¬ â€“  
- Water â†’ Ice â†’ Steam  
(Composition á€á€°á€Šá€®á€•á€±á€™á€²á€· Phase á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹)

---

## **2. Phases of Matter**

- **Solid Phase** â†’ Definite shape & volume  
- **Liquid Phase** â†’ Definite volume only  
- **Vapor/Gas Phase** â†’ No definite shape or volume  

Thermodynamics á€™á€¾á€¬á€á€±á€¬á€·  
Phase Change á€•á€¼á€¯á€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€á€Šá€·á€º Substances (Steam, Refrigerant, etc.) á€¡á€•á€±á€«á€º á€¡á€á€¼á€±á€á€¶á€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **3. Phase Change Process of Pure Substance**

Typical Example â€“ *Water (Hâ‚‚O)*  
Process: Heating under constant pressure.

### **Stage Description:**

| Stage | Description | Property |
|--------|--------------|----------|
| Aâ€“B | **Compressed (Subcooled) Liquid** | Liquid only |
| Bâ€“C | **Saturated Liquid** | Ready to vaporize |
| Câ€“D | **Mixture (Liquid + Vapor)** | Phase Change Region |
| Dâ€“E | **Saturated Vapor** | Fully evaporated |
| Eâ€“F | **Superheated Vapor** | Above saturation temperature |

---

## **4. Saturation Temperature & Pressure**

- **Saturation Temperature (T_sat):**  
  â†’ Temperature at which phase change occurs at a given pressure.  
- **Saturation Pressure (P_sat):**  
  â†’ Pressure at which phase change occurs at a given temperature.

Relationship between T_sat and P_sat â‡’ **Vapor Pressure Curve**

---

## **5. Quality (x)**

Mixture Zone (Saturated Liquid + Vapor) á€™á€¾á€¬  
Dryness Fraction (Quality) á€€á€­á€¯ á€á€á€ºá€™á€¾á€á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹



x = (m_vapor) / (m_liquid + m_vapor)


**Range:**
- x = 0 â†’ Saturated Liquid  
- x = 1 â†’ Saturated Vapor  

Property calculation:


y = y_f + x (y_g - y_f)

where:
- y = property of mixture  
- y_f = saturated liquid value  
- y_g = saturated vapor value  

---

## **6. Enthalpy of Phase Change**

- **hf:** Enthalpy of Saturated Liquid  
- **hg:** Enthalpy of Saturated Vapor  
- **hfg:** Latent Heat of Vaporization = hg - hf  

For Mixture:  


h = hf + xÂ·hfg

## **8. Pressureâ€“Temperature (Pâ€“T) Diagram**

Phase Boundary Curve á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€™á€»á€­á€¯á€¸á€›á€¾á€­á€á€šá€ºá‹

| Curve | Description |
|--------|--------------|
| Sublimation Curve | Solid â†” Vapor |
| Fusion Curve | Solid â†” Liquid |
| Vaporization Curve | Liquid â†” Vapor |

**Triple Point:**  
Three phases exist simultaneously.  
**Critical Point:**  
Saturated liquid & vapor properties become identical.  

After critical point â†’ Supercritical Fluid (no clear distinction between liquid/vapor).

## **10. Compressed and Superheated States**

| Type | Description | Key Note |
|--------|--------------|----------|
| **Compressed (Subcooled) Liquid** | Liquid below T_sat at given P | h â‰ˆ h_f |
| **Superheated Vapor** | Vapor above T_sat at given P | h > h_g |

## **11. Steam Tables**

Steam Tables á€á€½á€„á€º Water / Steam Properties á€€á€­á€¯ P, T, v, u, h, s á€á€”á€ºá€–á€­á€¯á€¸á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€¡á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€‘á€¬á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

### **Types of Tables:**

| Property | Value |
|------------|---------|
| T_sat | 99.63Â°C |
| v_f | 0.001043 mÂ³/kg |
| v_g | 1.673 mÂ³/kg |
| h_f | 417.5 kJ/kg |
| h_g | 2675.5 kJ/kg |
| s_f | 1.303 kJ/kgÂ·K |
| s_g | 7.359 kJ/kgÂ·K |

## **12. Mollier Diagram (hâ€“s Diagram)**

hâ€“s Diagram á€Ÿá€¬ Steam Turbine, Nozzle, Compressor Analysis á€á€½á€±á€¡á€á€½á€€á€º á€¡á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

- Vertical lines â†’ Constant Pressure

- Sloping lines â†’ Constant Entropy (Isentropic Process)

**Use:** Quickly estimate enthalpy & efficiency during power plant calculations.

## **13. Phase Change Energy Calculations**

### **Heating of Water Example**
1. Heat water from 0Â°C to 100Â°C â†’ Sensible Heat  
2. Boil at 100Â°C â†’ Latent Heat (Phase Change)  
3. Heat vapor beyond 100Â°C â†’ Superheat

Total Heat Supplied:


Q_total = m(c_pÂ·Î”T_liquid + h_fg + c_pvÂ·Î”T_vapor)

Refrigerants á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€¡á€±á€¸á€á€”á€ºá€¸á€…á€€á€º, Air-conditioning á€…á€”á€…á€ºá€á€½á€„á€º

|-------|--------------------|--------------------|--------|

## **17. Real Substance vs Ideal Gas**

| Aspect | Ideal Gas | Real Substance |
|----------|-------------|----------------|
| Equation of State | PV = RT | Complex (Non-linear) |
| Phase Change | No | Yes |
| Compressibility Factor (Z) | = 1 | â‰  1 |
| Validity | High T, Low P | Near Phase Change Zones |

## **19. Saturation Dome Concept**

The **Saturation Dome** separates liquid, vapor, and two-phase regions.  
Left â†’ Compressed Liquid, Right â†’ Superheated Vapor.  
Inside Dome â†’ Quality (x) defines mixture ratio.

Entropy & Enthalpy variation across dome â†’ 
Smooth & Continuous, but Volume & Temperature show sharp changes.

# ğŸ”„ Chapter 7 â€“ Thermodynamic Cycles (Carnot, Rankine, Otto, Diesel, Brayton)

---

## **Overview**

Thermodynamic Cycle á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
System á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€Ÿá€¬ Continuous Process á€á€…á€ºá€œá€»á€¾á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€™á€¾á€¬  
Heat á€€á€­á€¯ Work á€¡á€–á€¼á€…á€º á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€•á€¼á€®á€¸ á€”á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€†á€¯á€¶á€¸á€¡á€á€»á€­á€”á€ºá€™á€¾á€¬  
Original State á€€á€­á€¯ á€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€›á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€œá€¬á€á€²á€· Closed Path á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

> In every thermodynamic cycle, **Heat Input â†’ Work Output â†’ Heat Rejection** takes place.

Cycle á€á€½á€±á€Ÿá€¬ Power Plant, Engine, Refrigeration, Gas Turbine á€…á€á€²á€·  
Real Machines á€á€½á€±á€›á€²á€· Idealized Representation á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **1. Classification of Thermodynamic Cycles**

| Type | Working Substance | Example |
|-------|--------------------|----------|
| **Gas Cycles** | Gas remains gas throughout | Otto, Diesel, Brayton |
| **Vapor Cycles** | Working fluid changes phase | Rankine, Refrigeration |
| **Reversible Cycles** | Ideal, frictionless | Carnot, Stirling |
| **Irreversible Cycles** | Realistic, with losses | Actual engines |

---

## **2. Carnot Cycle (Ideal Standard of Efficiency)**

### **Processes:**
1. **Isothermal Expansion (1â€“2):**  
   Heat absorbed from hot reservoir (Tâ‚).


Qâ‚ = Tâ‚Â·(Sâ‚‚ â€“ Sâ‚)

2. **Adiabatic Expansion (2â€“3):**  
No heat exchange, temperature drops from Tâ‚ â†’ Tâ‚‚.
3. **Isothermal Compression (3â€“4):**  
Heat rejected to cold reservoir.


Qâ‚‚ = Tâ‚‚Â·(Sâ‚ƒ â€“ Sâ‚„)

4. **Adiabatic Compression (4â€“1):**  
Temperature rises back to Tâ‚.

### **Efficiency:**


Î·_Carnot = 1 - (Tâ‚‚ / Tâ‚)


**Key Point:** Carnot cycle is reversible and represents the maximum possible efficiency between two temperature limits.

---

## **3. Rankine Cycle (Steam Power Plant Cycle)**

Used in â€“ Steam Turbines, Power Plants.

### **Processes:**
1. **1â€“2: Isentropic Expansion (Turbine)**  
   Steam expands producing work.
2. **2â€“3: Constant Pressure Heat Rejection (Condenser)**  
   Steam condenses to water.
3. **3â€“4: Isentropic Compression (Pump)**  
   Water is pumped to boiler pressure.
4. **4â€“1: Constant Pressure Heat Addition (Boiler)**  
   Water converted to steam.

### **Efficiency:**


Î· = (W_turbine - W_pump) / Q_in


**Improvement Methods:**
- Superheating the steam  
- Regeneration (feedwater heating)  
- Reheat cycle  

**Typical Efficiency:** 30â€“40%

---

## **4. Otto Cycle (Spark Ignition Engine)**

Used in â€“ Petrol Engines.

### **Processes:**
1. **1â€“2: Isentropic Compression**  
   Airâ€“fuel mixture compressed.
2. **2â€“3: Constant Volume Heat Addition**  
   Combustion occurs at constant volume.
3. **3â€“4: Isentropic Expansion (Power Stroke)**  
   Piston moves down producing work.
4. **4â€“1: Constant Volume Heat Rejection**

### **Efficiency:**


Î·_Otto = 1 - (1 / r^(Î³ - 1))


Where:
- r = Compression Ratio (Vâ‚/Vâ‚‚)
- Î³ = Cp/Cv

**Higher r â†’ Higher efficiency.**

---

## **5. Diesel Cycle (Compression Ignition Engine)**

Used in â€“ Diesel Engines, Heavy Vehicles.

### **Processes:**
1. **1â€“2: Isentropic Compression**  
   Only air compressed (high temperature).
2. **2â€“3: Constant Pressure Heat Addition**  
   Fuel injected â†’ burns â†’ expansion.
3. **3â€“4: Isentropic Expansion (Power Stroke)**  
   Work output.
4. **4â€“1: Constant Volume Heat Rejection**

### **Efficiency:**


Î·_Diesel = 1 - (1/r^(Î³ - 1)) * [(Ï^Î³ - 1) / (Î³(Ï - 1))]


Where:
- r = Compression ratio
- Ï = Cut-off ratio = Vâ‚ƒ/Vâ‚‚

**Diesel engines have higher compression ratios â†’ better fuel economy.**

---

## **6. Comparison of Otto and Diesel Cycles**

| Parameter | Otto Cycle | Diesel Cycle |
|------------|-------------|---------------|
| Heat Addition | Constant Volume | Constant Pressure |
| Compression Ratio | Lower (6â€“10) | Higher (12â€“22) |
| Efficiency | Higher (for same r) | Lower (for same r) |
| Engine Type | Spark Ignition | Compression Ignition |
| Fuel | Petrol | Diesel |

---

## **7. Dual Cycle (Mixed Cycle)**

Used in â€“ Modern Diesel Engines.

Combination of Otto and Diesel:
- Heat addition partly at constant volume, partly at constant pressure.

Efficiency lies between Otto & Diesel:


Î·_Dual = 1 - (1/r^(Î³ - 1)) * [(Î±Â·Ï^Î³ - 1) / (Î³Â·(Î± - 1 + Î³(Ï - 1)))]


---

## **8. Brayton Cycle (Gas Turbine Cycle)**

Used in â€“ Jet Engines, Gas Turbines.

### **Processes:**
1. **1â€“2: Isentropic Compression (Compressor)**
2. **2â€“3: Constant Pressure Heat Addition (Combustor)**
3. **3â€“4: Isentropic Expansion (Turbine)**
4. **4â€“1: Constant Pressure Heat Rejection**

### **Efficiency:**


Î·_Brayton = 1 - (1 / r_p^((Î³ - 1)/Î³))


Where:
- r_p = Pressure Ratio = Pâ‚‚/Pâ‚

**Typical Efficiency:** 30â€“35%

**Improvements:**
- Regeneration  
- Intercooling  
- Reheating  

---

## **9. Comparison of Cycles**

| Cycle | Working Fluid | Heat Addition | Used In | Efficiency Range |
|--------|----------------|----------------|----------|-------------------|
| Carnot | Theoretical | Isothermal | Ideal Benchmark | Highest |
| Rankine | Steam | Constant Pressure | Power Plant | 30â€“40% |
| Otto | Air-Fuel Mix | Constant Volume | Petrol Engine | 25â€“30% |
| Diesel | Air + Fuel | Constant Pressure | Diesel Engine | 30â€“35% |
| Brayton | Gas | Constant Pressure | Gas Turbine | 30â€“35% |

---

## **10. Real vs Ideal Cycle**

| Factor | Ideal Cycle | Real Cycle |
|----------|---------------|-------------|
| Friction | None | Present |
| Heat Loss | Ignored | Exists |
| Combustion | Instantaneous | Time-dependent |
| Efficiency | Maximum (Reversible) | Lower (Irreversible) |

---

## **11. Regeneration and Reheat**

**Regeneration:**  
Uses exhaust heat to preheat the feedwater â†’ increases efficiency.

**Reheat:**  
Steam expanded partially, reheated, and expanded again â†’ reduces moisture at turbine exit.

---

## **12. Combined Cycles**

Power Plant Design á€™á€¾á€¬ Efficiency á€á€­á€¯á€¸á€–á€­á€¯á€·  
Rankine + Brayton Cycle á€á€½á€± á€•á€±á€«á€„á€ºá€¸á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€á€á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

> Example: Gas Turbine (Brayton) exhaust â†’ Heat Recovery Boiler (Rankine).

**Combined Cycle Efficiency:** 55â€“60%  
Higher than individual cycles.

---

## **13. Refrigeration and Heat Pump Cycles**

- **Refrigeration Cycle:**  
  Absorbs heat from low temperature region â†’ rejects to high temperature.  
  (Reverse Rankine or Vapor-Compression Cycle)

- **Heat Pump:**  
  Same principle, but heat rejected to warm space (for heating).

**Coefficient of Performance (COP):**


COP_ref = Q_L / W
COP_hp = Q_H / W = COP_ref + 1


---

## **14. Tâ€“s Diagrams (General)**

| Cycle | Heat Addition | Heat Rejection |
|--------|----------------|----------------|
| Carnot | Horizontal (Isothermal) | Horizontal (Isothermal) |
| Rankine | Constant Pressure | Constant Pressure |
| Otto | Vertical (Const. Volume) | Vertical (Const. Volume) |
| Diesel | Sloped (Const. Pressure) | Vertical |
| Brayton | Horizontal | Horizontal |

---

## **15. Key Performance Parameters**

| Symbol | Meaning | Units |
|----------|-----------|--------|
| Î· | Efficiency | % |
| r | Compression Ratio | Dimensionless |
| Ï | Cut-off Ratio | Dimensionless |
| r_p | Pressure Ratio | Dimensionless |
| COP | Coefficient of Performance | Ratio |
| W_net | Net Work Output | kJ/kg |

---

## **16. Energy Conversion in Real Systems**

| Application | Cycle Type | Working Fluid | Efficiency |
|---------------|-------------|----------------|--------------|
| Thermal Power Plant | Rankine | Steam | 35â€“40% |
| Jet Engine | Brayton | Air | 30â€“35% |
| Automobile Engine | Otto / Diesel | Air-Fuel | 25â€“35% |
| Combined Cycle | Brayton + Rankine | Gas + Steam | 55â€“60% |
| Refrigerator | Reverse Rankine | Refrigerant | COP = 2â€“5 |

- Efficiency evaluation  
- Waste heat recovery analysis  
- Comparison between real & theoretical machines

> Thermodynamic cycles á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€™á€Šá€ºá€á€Šá€·á€º Energy Conversion System á€™á€†á€­á€¯  
> á€¡á€á€¼á€±á€á€¶ Principle á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  
> Carnot cycle á€á€Šá€º Efficiency á€¡á€™á€¼á€„á€·á€ºá€†á€¯á€¶á€¸á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸áŠ

**á€¡á€€á€»á€‰á€ºá€¸á€á€»á€¯á€•á€º:**
> â€œAll practical engines are imperfect versions of the Carnot cycle.  
> Understanding each cycle helps engineers design efficient power and refrigeration systems.â€


á€’á€®á€¡á€á€”á€ºá€¸á€”á€²á€·á€¡á€á€° Power Cycles á€›á€²á€· á€¡á€“á€­á€€ á€á€˜á€±á€¬á€á€›á€¬á€¸á€á€½á€±

# â„ï¸ Chapter 8 â€“ Refrigeration & Heat Pump Systems  
*(Vapor Compression, Absorption, Gas Refrigeration)*

---

## **Overview**

Refrigeration System á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
Low Temperature Region á€™á€¾ Heat á€€á€­á€¯ á€á€šá€ºá€šá€°á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
High Temperature Region á€‘á€²á€á€­á€¯á€· á€á€šá€ºá€•á€­á€¯á€·á€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€· á€…á€”á€…á€º á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

> â€œRefrigeration is the process of removing heat from a low-temperature space and rejecting it to a high-temperature sink.â€

Heat Pump System á€á€Šá€º á€á€°á€Šá€®á€á€Šá€·á€º Principle á€•á€±á€«á€ºá€™á€¾á€¬ á€¡á€á€¼á€±á€á€¶á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
á€¡á€•á€°á€€á€­á€¯ á€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€‘á€¯á€á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€· á€¡á€•á€°á€•á€±á€¸á€…á€€á€º á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **1. Basic Terminology**

| Term | Meaning | Unit |
|-------|-----------|------|
| **Refrigeration Effect** | Heat absorbed from low-temperature space | kJ/kg |
| **COP (Coefficient of Performance)** | Efficiency of Refrigeration System | Dimensionless |
| **Refrigerant** | Working fluid that absorbs & releases heat | â€” |
| **Ton of Refrigeration (TR)** | 1 TR = 3.517 kW = 211 kJ/min | â€” |

---

## **2. Principle of Refrigeration**

Refrigeration System á€á€Šá€º Carnot Cycle á Reversed Version á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

### **Reversed Carnot Cycle:**
1. **1â€“2:** Isentropic Compression  
2. **2â€“3:** Isothermal Heat Rejection  
3. **3â€“4:** Isentropic Expansion  
4. **4â€“1:** Isothermal Heat Absorption  

**COP (Coefficient of Performance):**


COP_R = T_L / (T_H - T_L)


Where:
- T_L = Temperature of cold region (K)  
- T_H = Temperature of hot region (K)

---

## **3. Types of Refrigeration Systems**

| Type | Working Principle | Example |
|--------|--------------------|----------|
| **Vapor Compression System (VCS)** | Compression, Condensation, Expansion, Evaporation | Domestic Refrigerator |
| **Vapor Absorption System (VAS)** | Absorption of refrigerant by absorbent | Ammoniaâ€“Water System |
| **Gas Refrigeration System** | Work of gas expansion | Aircraft cooling |
| **Thermoelectric / Magnetic Systems** | Peltier or Magnetic Effect | Cryogenic Systems |

---

## **4. Vapor Compression Refrigeration System (VCRS)**

**Most common system** used in domestic & industrial refrigeration.

### **Main Components:**
1. **Evaporator:**  
   Absorbs heat from refrigerated space â†’ Liquid refrigerant evaporates.

2. **Compressor:**  
   Increases vapor pressure & temperature.

3. **Condenser:**  
   Hot vapor releases heat to atmosphere â†’ Condenses into liquid.

4. **Expansion Valve (Throttle):**  
   Reduces pressure â†’ liquid partially evaporates.

---

### **Cycle Description (on pâ€“h or Tâ€“s diagram):**

1. **1â€“2:** Isentropic Compression (Compressor)  
2. **2â€“3:** Constant Pressure Heat Rejection (Condenser)  
3. **3â€“4:** Throttling (Expansion Valve)  
4. **4â€“1:** Constant Pressure Heat Absorption (Evaporator)

---

### **Performance (COP):**


COP_R = Q_L / W = (hâ‚ - hâ‚„) / (hâ‚‚ - hâ‚)


Where:
- hâ‚ = Enthalpy at evaporator outlet  
- hâ‚‚ = Enthalpy at compressor outlet  
- hâ‚ƒ = Enthalpy at condenser outlet  
- hâ‚„ = Enthalpy after expansion valve  

---

### **Ideal vs Actual VCRS**

| Parameter | Ideal | Actual |
|-------------|--------|---------|
| Compression | Isentropic | Polytropic |
| Pressure Drop | Neglected | Present |
| Superheating | None | Exists |
| Subcooling | None | Exists |

---

## **5. Subcooling and Superheating**

- **Subcooling:** Cooling the liquid refrigerant below its condensation temperature.  
  â†’ Increases refrigeration effect.

- **Superheating:** Heating the vapor above its saturation temperature.  
  â†’ Protects compressor (no liquid entry).

---

## **6. Types of Compressors**

| Type | Description | Used In |
|--------|--------------|----------|
| **Reciprocating** | Piston type, intermittent flow | Domestic Refrigerator |
| **Rotary** | Compact, continuous flow | AC systems |
| **Centrifugal** | High capacity, dynamic type | Industrial plants |

---

## **7. Common Refrigerants**

| Name | Formula | Type | Remarks |
|--------|------------|--------|----------|
| **R-22** | CHClFâ‚‚ | HCFC | Phased out |
| **R-134a** | Câ‚‚Hâ‚‚Fâ‚„ | HFC | CFC-free |
| **R-717** | NHâ‚ƒ | Natural | Toxic but efficient |
| **R-600a** | Câ‚„Hâ‚â‚€ | Hydrocarbon | Eco-friendly |
| **R-290** | Câ‚ƒHâ‚ˆ | Propane | High efficiency |

**Selection Criteria:**
- Low Ozone Depletion Potential (ODP)  
- Low Global Warming Potential (GWP)  
- Safe operating pressure  

---

## **8. Vapor Absorption Refrigeration System (VARS)**

VARS uses **heat energy** (instead of mechanical energy) to circulate refrigerant.

### **Main Components:**
1. **Evaporator:** Produces refrigerant vapor.  
2. **Absorber:** Absorbs vapor into absorbent liquid.  
3. **Pump:** Increases pressure of liquid mixture.  
4. **Generator:** Heat source separates refrigerant vapor.  
5. **Condenser:** Vapor condensed into liquid.  
6. **Expansion Valve:** Pressure reduction before evaporator.

---

### **Working Pair Examples:**
| Refrigerant | Absorbent | Application |
|---------------|------------|---------------|
| **NHâ‚ƒ** | Water | Industrial refrigeration |
| **Water** | LiBr | Air conditioning systems |

---

### **Advantages:**
- Uses low-grade heat (solar, exhaust gas).  
- Less mechanical components â†’ low noise.  
- Reliable for remote/off-grid applications.

### **Disadvantages:**
- Low COP (~0.6â€“0.8)  
- Large system size  
- Corrosion issues  

---

## **9. Gas Refrigeration System**

Used mainly in **Aircraft Cooling Systems.**

### **Cycle (Reversed Brayton or Bellâ€“Coleman Cycle):**
1. **1â€“2:** Isentropic Compression  
2. **2â€“3:** Constant Pressure Heat Rejection  
3. **3â€“4:** Isentropic Expansion  
4. **4â€“1:** Constant Pressure Heat Absorption  

### **COP:**


COP_R = T_L / (T_H - T_L)


**Characteristics:**
- No phase change  
- Simple, light-weight system  
- Low efficiency (COP â‰ˆ 0.3â€“0.5)

---

## **10. Comparison of Refrigeration Systems**

| Type | Energy Input | COP | Remarks |
|--------|----------------|------|----------|
| Vapor Compression | Mechanical (Compressor) | 2â€“5 | Most common |
| Vapor Absorption | Heat (Generator) | 0.6â€“0.8 | Quiet, eco-friendly |
| Gas Refrigeration | Mechanical (Air) | 0.3â€“0.5 | Aircraft use |

---

## **11. Heat Pump System**

> â€œA heat pump transfers heat from a low-temperature region to a high-temperature region using external work.â€

### **Performance:**


COP_HP = Q_H / W = (Q_L + W) / W = COP_R + 1


**Example:**  
Room Heater â†’ absorbs heat from outdoor air, releases indoors.

---

## **12. Cascade Refrigeration System**

Used for **very low temperatures** (Cryogenics, LNG, etc.)

Two or more VCRS systems connected in series:
- High-stage refrigerant condenses low-stage refrigerant.
- Each stage uses a different refrigerant suited for that temperature range.

---

## **13. Multistage Compression Systems**

Used when **large pressure ratios** are required.
- Reduces compressor work.
- Improves COP.
- Common in industrial chillers.

---

## **14. Performance Evaluation**

| Parameter | Symbol | Formula |
|-------------|-----------|----------|
| COP (Refrigeration) | COP_R | Q_L / W |
| COP (Heat Pump) | COP_HP | Q_H / W |
| Energy Efficiency Ratio (EER) | â€” | COP_R Ã— 3.412 |
| Work of Compressor | W | hâ‚‚ - hâ‚ |
| Refrigeration Effect | Q_L | hâ‚ - hâ‚„ |

---

## **15. Environmental Considerations**

- **ODP (Ozone Depletion Potential)** â†’ Should be as low as possible.  
- **GWP (Global Warming Potential)** â†’ Indicates greenhouse impact.  
- **Eco-friendly Alternatives:**  
  R-600a, R-290, R-717 (NHâ‚ƒ), COâ‚‚, HFO-1234yf.

---

## **16. Real vs Ideal Cycle Losses**

| Source of Loss | Effect |
|------------------|--------|
| Compressor Inefficiency | Increases work input |
| Throttling Loss | Reduces COP |
| Pressure Drops | Reduces refrigeration effect |
| Heat Leak | Increases load |

---

| Heat Pump | Heating Systems, Water Heaters |

# ğŸ”¥ Chapter 9 â€“ Gas Power Cycles  
*(Real Gas Turbine, Jet Propulsion, Intercooling, Regeneration, Reheating)*

---

## **Overview**

Gas Power Cycles á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€Ÿá€¬ Air (á€á€­á€¯á€·á€™á€Ÿá€¯á€á€º Gas) á€€á€­á€¯ Working Substance á€¡á€”á€±á€”á€²á€· á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Heat Energy á€€á€­á€¯ Mechanical Work á€¡á€–á€¼á€…á€º á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€· á€…á€”á€…á€º á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

> â€œA gas power cycle converts thermal energy of a gas into useful mechanical power through cyclic processes.â€

á€¡á€“á€­á€€ á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€á€²á€· Cycles á€á€½á€±á€€á€á€±á€¬á€· â€“  
**Otto**, **Diesel**, **Brayton (Gas Turbine)**, **Dual**, **Stirling**, **Ericsson** á€…á€á€²á€· Cycle á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  

á€’á€®á€¡á€á€”á€ºá€¸á€™á€¾á€¬á€á€±á€¬á€· Industrial Gas Turbine Systems á€”á€²á€·  
Jet Propulsion Systems á€¡á€•á€±á€«á€º á€¡á€á€¼á€±á€á€¶á€‘á€¬á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **1. Basic Principle of Gas Power Cycle**

Cycle á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€…á€®á€¸á€•á€¼á€®á€¸á€á€²á€·á€¡á€á€«á€™á€¾á€¬  
System á€Ÿá€¬ Initial State á€€á€­á€¯ á€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€›á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€œá€¬á€•á€¼á€®á€¸ Work Net Output á€›á€¾á€­á€›á€™á€šá€ºá‹

**Net Work Done:**


W_net = W_expansion - W_compression


**Thermal Efficiency:**


Î· = W_net / Q_in


---

## **2. Brayton Cycle (Ideal Gas Turbine Cycle)**

Brayton Cycle á€€á€­á€¯ **J.P. Joule** á€€á€–á€±á€¬á€ºá€•á€¼á€á€²á€·á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Gas Turbine Engine á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€á€½á€„á€º á€¡á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€¡á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€†á€¯á€¶á€¸ á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

### **Processes:**

1. **1â€“2: Isentropic Compression (Compressor)**  
   Air compressed â†’ pressure & temperature rise.

2. **2â€“3: Constant Pressure Heat Addition (Combustion Chamber)**  
   Fuel added â†’ combustion occurs.

3. **3â€“4: Isentropic Expansion (Turbine)**  
   High-temperature gas expands â†’ Work output.

4. **4â€“1: Constant Pressure Heat Rejection**  
   Exhaust gas released â†’ cycle completed.

---

### **Efficiency Formula:**

For Ideal Gas (Air-standard assumption):



Î·_Brayton = 1 - (1 / r_p^((Î³ - 1)/Î³))


Where:
- r_p = Pressure Ratio (Pâ‚‚/Pâ‚)
- Î³ = Specific Heat Ratio (Cp/Cv)

---

### **Key Points:**
- Efficiency â†‘ when Pressure Ratio â†‘  
- Work output depends on Turbine & Compressor temperature difference.  
- Used in Aircraft Jet Engines, Power Plants.

---

## **3. Tâ€“s and Pâ€“v Diagrams**



T-s Diagram:
3
|
|
2 | \ 4
|
1----> s


- 1â€“2: Compression  
- 2â€“3: Heat Addition  
- 3â€“4: Expansion  
- 4â€“1: Heat Rejection  

---

## **4. Real Gas Turbine Cycle**

In practice, losses occur â†’  
Compressor not perfectly isentropic, turbine not ideal, pressure drops occur.

### **Actual Cycle Features:**
- Compressor efficiency (Î·_c): 80â€“90%  
- Turbine efficiency (Î·_t): 85â€“90%  
- Pressure losses in combustion chamber (2â€“5%)  
- Reduced net work output

---

### **Actual Efficiency:**


Î·_actual = Î·_t Ã— Î·_c Ã— Î·_Brayton


---

## **5. Cycle Improvements**

To increase efficiency or power output, following methods used:

| Method | Function | Effect |
|---------|-----------|---------|
| **Regeneration** | Recover heat from exhaust | â†‘ Efficiency |
| **Reheating** | Expand in multiple turbines | â†‘ Power Output |
| **Intercooling** | Multi-stage compression | â†“ Compressor Work |
| **Combination** | Using all three | â†‘ Efficiency & Power |

---

## **6. Regeneration**

> Uses exhaust gas heat to preheat compressed air before combustion.

### **Working Principle:**
Hot exhaust gas â†’ Regenerator â†’ transfers heat â†’ incoming compressed air.

**Regenerative Efficiency:**


Î·_reg = (T5 - T2) / (T4 - T2)


**Effect:**
- Reduces fuel consumption  
- Increases overall cycle efficiency  

---

## **7. Intercooling**

> Multi-stage compression reduces compressor work.

### **Process:**
Air compressed in two or more stages â†’ cooled by intercooler between stages.

**Advantages:**
- Reduced work input  
- Smaller compressor power requirement  

**Disadvantages:**
- Reduced turbine inlet temperature â†’ may reduce efficiency if not properly designed.

---

## **8. Reheating**

> Expanding gas in two or more turbines separated by a reheater.

### **Process:**
After first turbine expansion â†’ gas reheated â†’ expanded again in second turbine.

**Advantages:**
- Increases net work output  
- Reduces exhaust moisture in steam cycles  

**Disadvantages:**
- Slightly lower overall efficiency  
- Increased system complexity

---

## **9. Combined Effect: Intercooling + Regeneration + Reheating**

Used in **High-performance Gas Turbines**.

**Benefits:**
- High efficiency (up to 50%)  
- Better power output  
- Stable temperature levels  

**Applications:**  
Aircraft Propulsion, Combined Cycle Power Plants.

---

## **10. Jet Propulsion and Turbojet Engine**

> Jet Engine = Continuous Brayton Cycle used for producing thrust instead of shaft work.

---

### **Components of Jet Engine:**

1. **Inlet Diffuser** â€“ slows down air, increases pressure.  
2. **Compressor** â€“ increases air pressure.  
3. **Combustion Chamber** â€“ fuel burned, temperature rises.  
4. **Turbine** â€“ extracts work to drive compressor.  
5. **Nozzle** â€“ accelerates exhaust gases â†’ produces thrust.

---

### **Thrust (F):**


F = á¹(V_exit - V_inlet)


**Power Output:**


P = F Ã— V_flight


**Thermal Efficiency (Î·_th):**


Î·_th = (Work Output) / (Heat Supplied)


**Propulsive Efficiency (Î·_p):**


Î·_p = (2V) / (V + V_exit)


**Overall Efficiency (Î·_o):**


Î·_o = Î·_th Ã— Î·_p


---

## **11. Types of Jet Engines**

| Type | Working Principle | Used In |
|--------|-------------------|----------|
| **Turbojet** | Air + Fuel combustion, exhaust gases produce thrust | Fighter aircraft |
| **Turbofan** | Bypass air + Jet exhaust | Commercial aircraft |
| **Turboprop** | Turbine drives propeller | Small aircraft |
| **Ramjet / Scramjet** | High-speed airflow, no compressor | Hypersonic flight |

---

## **12. Jet Propulsion vs Gas Turbine**

| Feature | Jet Propulsion | Gas Turbine |
|-----------|----------------|---------------|
| Output | Thrust | Shaft Power |
| Working Medium | Air | Air / Combustion Gas |
| Application | Aircraft | Power Plant |
| Efficiency | High at high speed | High at constant load |

---

## **13. Combined Cycle Power Plants**

> Combine Brayton (Gas) + Rankine (Steam) cycles to recover exhaust heat.

**Gas Turbine Exhaust â†’ Heat Recovery Steam Generator (HRSG) â†’ Steam Turbine.**

**Advantages:**
- Efficiency up to 60%  
- Better fuel utilization  
- Lower emissions  

---

## **14. Typical Data for Gas Turbine**

| Parameter | Symbol | Typical Value |
|-------------|-----------|----------------|
| Pressure Ratio | r_p | 10â€“20 |
| Turbine Inlet Temperature | Tâ‚ƒ | 1000â€“1400Â°C |
| Turbine Efficiency | Î·_t | 0.88 |
| Compressor Efficiency | Î·_c | 0.85 |
| Overall Efficiency | Î·_o | 0.35â€“0.40 |

---

## **15. Comparison of Air-standard Cycles**

| Cycle | Heat Addition | Heat Rejection | Efficiency Range | Use |
|--------|----------------|----------------|------------------|------|
| Otto | Constant Volume | Constant Volume | 25â€“30% | Petrol Engines |
| Diesel | Constant Pressure | Constant Volume | 30â€“35% | Diesel Engines |
| Dual | Mixed | Constant Volume | 30â€“35% | Heavy Engines |
| Brayton | Constant Pressure | Constant Pressure | 30â€“40% | Gas Turbines |

- **Variable Geometry Compressors**  
- **Multi-stage Turbines**

- NOx and COâ‚‚ emissions from combustion

# ğŸ”¥ Chapter 10 â€“ Heat Transfer  
*(Conduction, Convection, Radiation, and Heat Exchangers)*

## **Overview**

Heat Transfer á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
Temperature Difference á€›á€¾á€­á€á€²á€·á€¡á€á€«  
Energy (as Heat) á€Ÿá€¬ á€á€…á€ºá€”á€±á€›á€¬á€™á€¾ á€á€…á€ºá€”á€±á€›á€¬á€á€­á€¯á€· á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€á€½á€¬á€¸á€á€²á€· Natural Process á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

> â€œHeat always flows spontaneously from a region of higher temperature to a region of lower temperature.â€

Thermodynamics á€€ Energy Conservation á€€á€­á€¯ á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€á€šá€ºá‹  
Heat Transfer á€€á€á€±á€¬á€· **Energy Transfer Rate (Speed)** á€€á€­á€¯ á€…á€‰á€ºá€¸á€…á€¬á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

## **1. Modes of Heat Transfer**

| Mode | Medium Required? | Mechanism | Example |
|-------|-------------------|-------------|-----------|
| **Conduction** | Solid, Liquid, Gas | Molecular vibration | Metal rod heating |
| **Convection** | Liquid, Gas | Fluid motion | Boiling water |
| **Radiation** | No medium | Electromagnetic waves | Sunlight |

---

## **2. Conduction**

> Transfer of heat within a stationary medium (solid or fluid) due to temperature gradient.

### **Fourierâ€™s Law of Heat Conduction:**


q = -k Â· A Â· (dT/dx)


Where:
- q = Heat transfer rate (W)  
- k = Thermal Conductivity (W/mÂ·K)  
- A = Area normal to heat flow (mÂ²)  
- dT/dx = Temperature gradient (K/m)

**Negative sign** â†’ Heat flows from high T to low T.

---

### **Thermal Conductivity (k)**

| Material | Thermal Conductivity (W/mÂ·K) |
|-----------|------------------------------|
| Copper | 385 |
| Aluminum | 205 |
| Steel | 50 |
| Glass | 0.8 |
| Air | 0.025 |

High k â†’ Good conductor (Metals)  
Low k â†’ Insulator (Wood, Air)

---

### **Steady-State Heat Conduction:**

For **Plane Wall** of thickness L:


Q = kA(Tâ‚ - Tâ‚‚)/L


For **Cylindrical Wall (Pipe)**:


Q = (2Ï€kL(Tâ‚ - Tâ‚‚)) / ln(râ‚‚/râ‚)


For **Spherical Wall**:


Q = (4Ï€k(Tâ‚ - Tâ‚‚)) / ((1/râ‚) - (1/râ‚‚))


---

### **Thermal Resistance Concept**

Equivalent to Electrical Resistance.



R_th = L / (kA)


Thus:


Q = Î”T / R_th


**Composite Walls:**  
Series or Parallel resistances used depending on layer arrangement.

---

## **3. Convection**

> Transfer of heat between a solid surface and a moving fluid due to temperature difference.

### **Newtonâ€™s Law of Cooling:**


q = hA(T_s - T_âˆ)


Where:
- h = Convective Heat Transfer Coefficient (W/mÂ²Â·K)  
- T_s = Surface temperature  
- T_âˆ = Fluid temperature  

---

### **Types of Convection**

| Type | Cause | Example |
|-------|--------|----------|
| **Natural (Free)** | Density differences due to temperature | Air near heater rises |
| **Forced** | Fluid forced by fan or pump | Cooling in car radiator |

---

### **Typical h Values:**

| Type | h (W/mÂ²Â·K) |
|--------|--------------|
| Free convection (air) | 5â€“25 |
| Forced convection (air) | 25â€“250 |
| Boiling (water) | 2000â€“100,000 |
| Condensation (steam) | 5000â€“50,000 |

---

### **Dimensionless Numbers**

| Symbol | Name | Formula | Purpose |
|----------|--------|-----------|----------|
| Re | Reynolds Number | ÏVD/Î¼ | Flow regime |
| Pr | Prandtl Number | Î¼Cp/k | Fluid property |
| Nu | Nusselt Number | hD/k | Heat transfer coefficient |
| Gr | Grashof Number | gÎ²Î”T LÂ³/Î½Â² | Natural convection |

---

## **4. Radiation**

> Transfer of heat by electromagnetic waves, does not require medium.

### **Stefanâ€“Boltzmann Law:**


q = Ïƒ Tâ´

Where:
- Ïƒ = 5.67 Ã— 10â»â¸ W/mÂ²Â·Kâ´

For a real surface (emissivity Îµ):


q = ÎµÏƒTâ´


---

### **Radiation Between Two Surfaces:**



Q = ÎµÏƒA(Tâ‚â´ - Tâ‚‚â´)


**Emissivity (Îµ):**  
0 â‰¤ Îµ â‰¤ 1  
Polished surface â†’ Îµ = 0.05  
Blackbody â†’ Îµ = 1.0

---

### **Key Radiation Terms**

| Term | Description |
|--------|---------------|
| **Blackbody** | Perfect absorber & emitter |
| **Graybody** | Constant emissivity < 1 |
| **Reflectivity (Ï)** | Fraction of radiation reflected |
| **Absorptivity (Î±)** | Fraction absorbed |
| **Transmissivity (Ï„)** | Fraction transmitted |

Relation:


Î± + Ï + Ï„ = 1


---

## **5. Combined Heat Transfer**

In many real systems â†’ multiple modes occur simultaneously.

**Example:**  
Wall exposed to hot gas â†’ Convection + Conduction + Radiation.

**Overall Heat Transfer Coefficient (U):**


Q = U A Î”T


Where:


1/U = 1/hâ‚ + (L/k) + 1/hâ‚‚


---

## **6. Transient Heat Conduction**

> Temperature changes with time as well as position.

**Governing Equation (1D):**


âˆ‚T/âˆ‚t = (Î±) âˆ‚Â²T/âˆ‚xÂ²


Where:
- Î± = Thermal diffusivity = k / (ÏCp)

**Lumped System Analysis:**
If Biot number (Bi = hL/k) < 0.1 â†’  
Object temperature assumed uniform.



T(t) = T_âˆ + (T_i - T_âˆ) e^(-(hA/ÏVCp)t)


---

## **7. Heat Exchangers**

> Devices used to transfer heat between two or more fluids at different temperatures.

---

### **Types of Heat Exchangers**

| Type | Flow Arrangement | Example |
|-------|-------------------|----------|
| **Parallel Flow** | Both fluids move same direction | Simple radiator |
| **Counter Flow** | Opposite directions | Condenser, Boiler |
| **Cross Flow** | Fluids cross perpendicularly | Air coolers |

---

### **Performance Parameters**

| Parameter | Symbol | Formula |
|-------------|-----------|----------|
| Heat Transfer Rate | Q | m Cp (T_in - T_out) |
| Log Mean Temperature Difference (LMTD) | Î”T_lm | (Î”Tâ‚ - Î”Tâ‚‚)/ln(Î”Tâ‚/Î”Tâ‚‚) |
| Effectiveness | Îµ | Q_actual / Q_max |

---

### **Overall Heat Transfer Coefficient (U):**



1/U = 1/h_hot + (Î”x/k_wall) + 1/h_cold


**Typical Values:**
- Gasâ€“Gas: 10â€“100 W/mÂ²Â·K  
- Gasâ€“Liquid: 100â€“1000  
- Liquidâ€“Liquid: 500â€“5000  
- Condensing Steam: 5000â€“20,000  

---

### **Compact Heat Exchangers:**
Used where space is limited (e.g., aircraft systems).  
High surface area per volume (A/V > 700 mÂ²/mÂ³).

---

## **8. Boiling and Condensation**

### **Boiling Heat Transfer:**
Occurs when liquid contacts surface above saturation temperature.

Types:
- Natural Convection Boiling  
- Nucleate Boiling (efficient)  
- Film Boiling (inefficient)

### **Condensation:**
Vapor â†’ Liquid phase on cooler surface.

| Type | Description |
|--------|--------------|
| **Film Condensation** | Continuous liquid film (low h) |
| **Dropwise Condensation** | Discrete droplets (high h) |

---

## **9. Thermal Insulation and Lagging**

> Reduces heat loss or gain from systems.

Used in â€“ Boilers, Refrigeration, Piping, Cold Storage.

**Effective insulation:** Low thermal conductivity, moisture resistant.

---

## **10. Extended Surfaces (Fins)**

> Increase surface area â†’ enhance convection.

**Heat Transfer Rate:**


Q = âˆš(hPkA(T_base - T_âˆ)) tanh(mL)


**Fin Efficiency (Î·_f):**


Î·_f = (Actual Heat Transfer) / (Maximum Possible)


Used in radiators, motor cooling, heat sinks.

---

## **11. Heat Exchanger Design Methods**

### **1. LMTD Method:**


Q = U A Î”T_lm

Used when inlet/outlet temperatures known.

### **2. Effectivenessâ€“NTU Method:**


Îµ = f(NTU, C_r)

Used when outlet temperatures unknown.

Where:
- NTU = UA / C_min  
- C_r = C_min / C_max

---

## **12. Thermal Contact Resistance**

Occurs when two solid surfaces touch imperfectly â†’ air gaps reduce heat transfer.  
Minimized using greases or high-conductivity paste.

---

## **13. Radiation Shields**

Used to reduce radiant heat between surfaces (e.g., cryogenic tanks).  
Polished metal foils (Îµ â‰ˆ 0.05) are highly effective.

---

## **14. Typical Engineering Applications**

| System | Dominant Mode | Description |
|----------|----------------|---------------|
| Boiler tubes | Convection | Water-steam heat transfer |
| Condenser | Convection + Phase Change | Steam condenses to water |
| Engine Cooling | Forced Convection | Air/water removes heat |
| Building Insulation | Conduction | Thermal resistance |
| Solar Collector | Radiation | Absorbs solar heat |

| Parameter | Formula |
|-------------|-----------|
| Fourierâ€™s Law | q = -kA(dT/dx) |

## **17. Energy Balance in Heat Exchanger**



m_h Cp_h (T_hi - T_ho) = m_c Cp_c (T_co - T_ci)


No phase change assumed; if phase change, latent heat included.

---

## **18. Thermal Diffusivity**

> Ability of material to conduct thermal energy relative to its ability to store energy.



Î± = k / (ÏCp)


High Î± â†’ fast temperature equalization.

# ğŸ’§ Chapter 11 â€“ Fluid Mechanics & Flow Measurement  
*(Continuity, Bernoulli, Viscosity, Pipe Flow, Pumps, and Turbines)*

---

## **Overview**

Fluid Mechanics á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
Liquid á€”á€²á€· Gas (á€¡á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€†á€¯á€¶á€¸á€¡á€”á€±á€–á€¼á€„á€·á€º Water, Air) á€á€­á€¯á€·á€›á€²á€·  
Flow Behavior, Pressure, Velocity, Force, Energy transfer á€…á€á€²á€·  
á€•á€…á€¹á€…á€Šá€ºá€¸á€†á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€›á€¬ á€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€†á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€á€»á€€á€ºá€á€½á€±á€€á€­á€¯ á€œá€±á€·á€œá€¬á€á€²á€· á€á€®á€¡á€­á€¯á€›á€®á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

> â€œFluid Mechanics is the study of fluids in motion and at rest, and the forces acting on them.â€

---

## **1. Properties of Fluids**

| Property | Symbol | Unit | Description |
|------------|----------|--------|-------------|
| Density | Ï | kg/mÂ³ | Mass per unit volume |
| Specific Weight | Î³ | N/mÂ³ | Weight per unit volume (Ïg) |
| Specific Gravity | â€” | â€” | Ratio to water density |
| Viscosity | Î¼ | NÂ·s/mÂ² | Fluid resistance to motion |
| Kinematic Viscosity | Î½ | mÂ²/s | Î¼ / Ï |
| Compressibility | Î² | Paâ»Â¹ | Volume change due to pressure |

---

### **Viscosity (Î¼)**

> Internal friction in a fluid that resists relative motion between layers.

**Newtonâ€™s Law of Viscosity:**


Ï„ = Î¼ (du/dy)


Where:
- Ï„ = Shear stress (N/mÂ²)
- du/dy = Velocity gradient

**Newtonian Fluids:** Constant Î¼ (e.g. water, air)  
**Non-Newtonian Fluids:** Variable Î¼ (e.g. blood, paint)

---

## **2. Types of Fluid Flow**

| Type | Description | Example |
|--------|--------------|----------|
| **Steady Flow** | Parameters (V, P, Ï) constant w.r.t time | Flow in a straight pipe |
| **Unsteady Flow** | Parameters vary with time | Pulsating flow |
| **Uniform Flow** | Velocity same at all points | Flow in uniform pipe |
| **Non-uniform Flow** | Velocity changes with position | Nozzle flow |
| **Laminar Flow** | Smooth layers, orderly | Re < 2000 |
| **Turbulent Flow** | Random, eddies | Re > 4000 |
| **Compressible Flow** | Density varies (gases) | Jet flow |
| **Incompressible Flow** | Density constant | Liquids |

---

## **3. Continuity Equation**

> â€œMass cannot be created or destroyed within a control volume.â€

For incompressible steady flow:



Aâ‚Vâ‚ = Aâ‚‚Vâ‚‚


Where:
- A = Cross-sectional area  
- V = Velocity  

**Meaning:**  
If pipe diameter decreases â†’ velocity increases proportionally.

---

## **4. Bernoulliâ€™s Equation**

> Relationship between pressure, velocity, and elevation in steady, frictionless flow.



(P/Ïg) + (VÂ²/2g) + z = Constant


Where:
- P = Pressure energy per unit weight  
- VÂ²/2g = Kinetic energy per unit weight  
- z = Potential energy per unit weight  

**Interpretation:**  
Total energy per unit weight is constant along a streamline.

---

### **Bernoulliâ€™s Applications**

| Device | Working Principle | Purpose |
|----------|-------------------|-----------|
| **Venturi Meter** | Pressure drop measures velocity | Flow rate measurement |
| **Orifice Meter** | Small opening creates pressure difference | Flow measurement |
| **Pitot Tube** | Measures stagnation & static pressure | Velocity measurement |

---

### **Discharge Formula for Venturi Meter:**


Q = C_d Aâ‚Aâ‚‚ / âˆš(Aâ‚Â² - Aâ‚‚Â²) âˆš(2gh)

Where:
- C_d = Coefficient of discharge (~0.98)
- h = Head difference (m)

---

## **5. Energy and Head Losses**

In real flow â†’ friction causes **head loss (h_f)**.

### **Darcyâ€“Weisbach Equation:**


h_f = f (L/D) (VÂ² / 2g)

Where:
- f = Friction factor  
- L = Length of pipe  
- D = Diameter  
- V = Velocity  

### **Friction Factor (f):**

| Flow Type | Expression |
|-------------|--------------|
| Laminar | f = 64/Re |
| Turbulent | f = 0.316/Reâ°Â·Â²âµ (for smooth pipe) |

---

### **Total Energy Line (TEL) & Hydraulic Grade Line (HGL):**
- **TEL:** P/Ïg + VÂ²/2g + z  
- **HGL:** P/Ïg + z  
Energy decreases due to friction losses along the flow.

---

## **6. Flow Through Pipes**

### **Series Pipes:**


h_total = hâ‚ + hâ‚‚ + hâ‚ƒ

Flow (Q) same in all.

### **Parallel Pipes:**


hâ‚ = hâ‚‚ = hâ‚ƒ

Total flow = Qâ‚ + Qâ‚‚ + Qâ‚ƒ

---

### **Equivalent Pipe:**
A single pipe giving same head loss and flow rate as multiple pipes:


L_e/D_eâµ = Lâ‚/Dâ‚âµ + Lâ‚‚/Dâ‚‚âµ + ...


---

## **7. Measurement of Flow**

### **Devices:**

| Device | Principle | Formula | Accuracy |
|-----------|-------------|-----------|------------|
| **Venturi Meter** | Bernoulliâ€™s Equation | Q = C_d Aâ‚Aâ‚‚ / âˆš(Aâ‚Â² - Aâ‚‚Â²) âˆš(2gh) | 98% |
| **Orifice Meter** | Pressure difference | Q = C_d A âˆš(2gh) | 60â€“80% |
| **Pitot Tube** | Velocity head | V = âˆš(2gh) | 95% |
| **Rotameter** | Variable area | Direct reading | 90â€“95% |

---

## **8. Dimensional Analysis**

> Used to derive relations between physical quantities.

### **Buckingham Ï€-Theorem:**
If a physical relation involves *n* variables and *m* fundamental dimensions,  
then (n - m) dimensionless groups (Ï€ terms) exist.



Ï€â‚ = f(Ï€â‚‚, Ï€â‚ƒ, â€¦)


**Common Dimensionless Numbers:**
- Reynolds Number (Re) = ÏVD/Î¼  
- Froude Number (Fr) = V / âˆš(gL)  
- Euler Number (Eu) = P / (ÏVÂ²)  
- Weber Number (We) = ÏVÂ²L / Ïƒ  

---

## **9. Boundary Layer Concept**

> Thin layer near solid surface where viscous effects dominate.

### **Thickness Definitions:**
- **Î´:** Velocity boundary layer  
- **Î´_t:** Thermal boundary layer  

**Boundary Layer Separation:**  
Occurs when adverse pressure gradient causes reverse flow â†’ drag â†‘.

---

## **10. Flow Over Notches and Weirs**

Used for open-channel flow measurement.

### **Rectangular Notch:**


Q = (2/3) C_d âˆš(2g) b HÂ³/Â²


### **V-Notch (Triangular):**


Q = (8/15) C_d âˆš(2g) tan(Î¸/2) Hâµ/Â²


---

## **11. Hydraulic Machines**

> Machines that convert energy between fluid and mechanical form.

| Type | Energy Conversion | Example |
|--------|--------------------|----------|
| **Turbines** | Fluid â†’ Mechanical | Hydro Turbines |
| **Pumps** | Mechanical â†’ Fluid | Centrifugal, Reciprocating |

---

## **12. Turbines**

### **Classification:**

| Type | Head | Flow | Example |
|--------|--------|--------|----------|
| **Pelton Wheel** | High (>250 m) | Impulse | Mountain regions |
| **Francis Turbine** | Medium (30â€“250 m) | Reaction | Hydropower plants |
| **Kaplan Turbine** | Low (<30 m) | Axial | Low-head dams |

---

### **Pelton Wheel (Impulse Turbine)**

**Working Principle:**  
Water jet from nozzle strikes buckets on runner â†’ impulse causes rotation.

**Power Output:**


P = ÏgQHÎ·

**Efficiency:**


Î·_h = (V_jet Ã— V_runner) / gH


---

### **Francis Turbine (Reaction Type)**

- Mixed flow â†’ part radial, part axial  
- Water enters via spiral casing  
- Adjustable guide vanes control flow  

**Efficiency:** 85â€“90%

---

### **Kaplan Turbine**

- Axial flow, propeller-type blades  
- Suitable for low head and high discharge  
**Efficiency:** 90â€“95%

---

## **13. Pumps**

### **Centrifugal Pump (Most Common)**

**Principle:**  
Dynamic energy from impeller converts to pressure energy.

**Head Developed:**


H = (Vâ‚‚Â² - Vâ‚Â²) / (2g)


**Manometric Efficiency:**


Î·_m = gH / (V_wâ‚‚ uâ‚‚)


---

### **Reciprocating Pump**

- Positive displacement  
- Delivers fixed volume per stroke  
- High pressure, low discharge  
**Used in:** hydraulic presses, injection systems

---

## **14. Pump and Turbine Similarity Laws**

| Quantity | Relation |
|-------------|------------|
| Flow rate | Q âˆ N DÂ³ |
| Head | H âˆ NÂ² DÂ² |
| Power | P âˆ NÂ³ Dâµ |

Where N = Speed, D = Diameter

---

## **15. Cavitation**

> Formation and collapse of vapor bubbles in low-pressure zones.

**Effects:**
- Noise and vibration  
- Metal erosion  
- Efficiency reduction  

**Prevention:**
- Increase suction head  
- Avoid very low pressures  
- Use proper impeller design

---

## **16. Hydraulic Efficiency Terms**

| Efficiency | Definition | Formula |
|--------------|--------------|-----------|
| **Volumetric (Î·_v)** | Actual / Theoretical discharge | Q_a / Q_t |
| **Mechanical (Î·_m)** | Output / Input power | P_out / P_in |
| **Overall (Î·_o)** | Î·_v Ã— Î·_m | â€” |

---

## **17. Specific Speed (N_s)**

Used to classify turbines/pumps.



N_s = N âˆšP / H^(5/4)


| Type | Ns Range |
|--------|-------------|
| Pelton | 10â€“35 |
| Francis | 60â€“300 |
| Kaplan | 300â€“1000 |

---

## **18. Flow Measurement in Open Channels**

| Device | Formula | Application |
|----------|-----------|--------------|
| **Venturi Flume** | Q = C âˆš(2gH) | Irrigation channels |
| **Weir (Rectangular, V-notch)** | Q âˆ HÂ³/Â² or Hâµ/Â² | Dams |
| **Current Meter** | V = kâ‚N + kâ‚‚ | Rivers |

## **19. Dimensionless Turbine Performance**

| Term | Formula |
|--------|-----------|
| Unit Speed | N_u = N / âˆšH |
| Unit Discharge | Q_u = Q / âˆšH |
| Unit Power | P_u = P / H^(3/2) |

Used for performance comparison under varying heads.

# ğŸš— Chapter 12 â€“ Internal Combustion Engines  
*(Otto, Diesel, Dual Cycles, Engine Performance, and Testing)*

---

## **Overview**

Internal Combustion Engine (IC Engine) á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
Fuel á€€á€­á€¯ Engine cylinder á€¡á€á€½á€„á€ºá€¸á€™á€¾á€¬ direct combustion á€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Chemical Energy á€€á€­á€¯ Mechanical Work á€¡á€–á€¼á€…á€º á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€· á€…á€”á€…á€º á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

> â€œAn Internal Combustion Engine converts the chemical energy of fuel into mechanical energy within the engine cylinder itself.â€

---

## **1. Classification of I.C. Engines**

| Basis | Type | Example |
|--------|--------|----------|
| **According to Fuel** | Petrol (Gasoline), Diesel, Gas | Car, Truck |
| **According to Cycle** | Otto, Diesel, Dual | SI, CI Engines |
| **According to Ignition** | Spark Ignition (SI), Compression Ignition (CI) | Cars, Trucks |
| **According to Stroke** | Two-stroke, Four-stroke | Motorbike, Car |
| **According to Cooling** | Air-cooled, Water-cooled | Motorcycle, Car |
| **According to Speed** | Low, Medium, High | Marine, Auto |

---

## **2. Basic Engine Components**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Cylinder** | Combustion chamber for fuelâ€“air mixture |
| **Piston** | Converts gas pressure into mechanical force |
| **Connecting Rod** | Connects piston to crankshaft |
| **Crankshaft** | Converts reciprocating motion into rotary motion |
| **Inlet Valve** | Allows air/fuel into cylinder |
| **Exhaust Valve** | Releases burnt gases |
| **Carburetor / Injector** | Supplies correct mixture of air and fuel |
| **Spark Plug / Fuel Injector** | Ignition device for SI / CI engines |

---

## **3. Working Principle of Four-Stroke Engine**

| Stroke | Function | Description |
|----------|-------------|--------------|
| **1. Suction (Intake)** | Inlet valve open | Piston moves down, draws in airâ€“fuel (SI) or air (CI) |
| **2. Compression** | Both valves closed | Piston moves up, compresses mixture |
| **3. Power (Expansion)** | Ignition occurs | Combustion â†’ expansion â†’ work output |
| **4. Exhaust** | Exhaust valve open | Burnt gases expelled |

**Four-stroke â†’ One power stroke per 2 revolutions of crankshaft.**

---

## **4. Two-Stroke Engine**

| Step | Action |
|--------|---------|
| **Downstroke** | Combustion gases expand, exhaust pushed out |
| **Upstroke** | Fresh charge enters via transfer port |

**Advantages:**  
- Simple design, light weight, one power stroke per revolution  
**Disadvantages:**  
- Lower efficiency, incomplete combustion, more noise

---

## **5. Otto Cycle (Petrol Engine Cycle)**

> Air-standard cycle for **Spark Ignition (SI)** engines.

### **Processes:**
1. **1â€“2:** Isentropic compression  
2. **2â€“3:** Constant volume heat addition  
3. **3â€“4:** Isentropic expansion  
4. **4â€“1:** Constant volume heat rejection  

**Efficiency:**


Î·_Otto = 1 - (1 / r^(Î³ - 1))


Where:
- r = Compression ratio (Vâ‚/Vâ‚‚)  
- Î³ = Cp/Cv  

**Typical efficiency:** 25â€“30%

---

## **6. Diesel Cycle (Compression Ignition Engine)**

> Used in **Diesel Engines**, fuel injected into compressed air.

### **Processes:**
1. **1â€“2:** Isentropic compression  
2. **2â€“3:** Constant pressure heat addition  
3. **3â€“4:** Isentropic expansion  
4. **4â€“1:** Constant volume heat rejection  

**Efficiency:**


Î·_Diesel = 1 - (1 / r^(Î³ - 1)) Ã— [(Ï^Î³ - 1)/(Î³(Ï - 1))]


Where:
- Ï = Cut-off ratio (Vâ‚ƒ/Vâ‚‚)

**Typical efficiency:** 30â€“35%

---

## **7. Dual Cycle**

> Combination of Otto & Diesel cycles (used in modern high-speed engines).

### **Heat Addition:**
- Partly at constant volume  
- Partly at constant pressure  

**Efficiency:**


Î·_Dual = 1 - (1 / r^(Î³ - 1)) Ã— [(Î± Ï^Î³ - 1)/((Î± - 1) + Î³ Î± (Ï - 1))]


Where:
- Î± = Pressure ratio (Pâ‚ƒ/Pâ‚‚)  
- Ï = Cut-off ratio (Vâ‚„/Vâ‚ƒ)

**Typical efficiency:** 32â€“36%

---

## **8. Comparison of Otto, Diesel, and Dual Cycles**

| Feature | Otto | Diesel | Dual |
|-----------|---------|---------|--------|
| Heat Addition | Constant volume | Constant pressure | Mixed |
| Compression Ratio | Low (6â€“10) | High (14â€“22) | Medium |
| Efficiency | 25â€“30% | 30â€“35% | 32â€“36% |
| Engine Type | SI | CI | CI (High-speed) |
| Fuel | Petrol | Diesel | Diesel / Gas |

---

## **9. Air-Fuel Mixture and Combustion**

| Engine Type | Mixture Type | Ignition |
|---------------|----------------|------------|
| **SI (Petrol)** | Homogeneous (Air + Fuel mixed) | Spark ignition |
| **CI (Diesel)** | Heterogeneous (Fuel injected) | Compression ignition |

**Stoichiometric Ratio:**  
Ideal airâ€“fuel ratio for complete combustion  
â‰ˆ 14.7 : 1 (Petrol)  
â‰ˆ 18 : 1 (Diesel)

---

## **10. Engine Performance Parameters**

| Parameter | Symbol | Formula | Description |
|-------------|----------|-----------|---------------|
| **Indicated Power (IP)** | â€” | (P_mi Ã— L Ã— A Ã— n Ã— K) / 60 | Power inside cylinder |
| **Brake Power (BP)** | â€” | (2Ï€NT) / 60 | Measured at crankshaft |
| **Mechanical Efficiency (Î·_m)** | â€” | BP / IP | Power transmitted ratio |
| **Brake Thermal Efficiency (Î·_bth)** | â€” | BP / (á¹_f Ã— CV) | Fuel-to-work efficiency |
| **Volumetric Efficiency (Î·_v)** | â€” | (Actual intake air / Theoretical) | Inlet filling efficiency |
| **Specific Fuel Consumption (SFC)** | â€” | á¹_f / BP | kg/kWh |
| **Mean Effective Pressure (IMEP)** | â€” | (IP Ã— 60) / (L Ã— A Ã— n) | Average pressure during power stroke |

---

## **11. Engine Testing**

### **Purpose:**
- Determine efficiency, power output, fuel consumption, heat balance, etc.

### **Testing Methods:**
1. **Morse Test (for multi-cylinder engines)**  
   - Disable one cylinder at a time â†’ measure BP drop â†’ calculate IP per cylinder.  

2. **Prony Brake / Rope Brake**  
   - Measure torque by frictional resistance.  

3. **Dynamometer Testing**  
   - **Hydraulic Dynamometer** (uses fluid resistance)  
   - **Eddy Current Dynamometer** (electromagnetic braking)

---

### **Brake Power from Dynamometer:**


BP = (2Ï€NT) / 60


---

## **12. Engine Heat Balance**

> Energy supplied by fuel = useful work + losses.



á¹_f Ã— CV = BP + Heat to cooling water + Heat to exhaust + Unaccounted losses


Typical distribution (Petrol Engine):
- Brake Power â†’ 25â€“30%  
- Cooling â†’ 30â€“35%  
- Exhaust â†’ 25â€“30%  
- Unaccounted â†’ 5â€“10%

---

## **13. Supercharging and Turbocharging**

| Type | Working Principle | Advantage |
|--------|--------------------|--------------|
| **Supercharger** | Driven by crankshaft | Increases air density, more power |
| **Turbocharger** | Driven by exhaust gases | Improves efficiency, no mechanical loss |

**Boost pressure:** 0.5â€“1.0 bar (typical)  

---

## **14. Engine Knock**

> Abnormal combustion producing sharp metallic sound.

| Engine Type | Cause | Remedy |
|---------------|----------|----------|
| **SI Engine Knock** | Auto-ignition of end gas | Higher octane fuel, cooling |
| **CI Engine Knock** | Delay in ignition | Lower cetane delay, better injection timing |

---

## **15. Engine Cooling Systems**

| Type | Medium | Application |
|--------|-----------|--------------|
| **Air Cooling** | Fins & fans | Motorcycles, aircraft |
| **Water Cooling** | Radiator, pump | Cars, generators |

**Purpose:** maintain optimum temperature (~90Â°C)

---

## **16. Lubrication System**

> Reduces friction between moving parts.

| Type | Description | Example |
|--------|---------------|------------|
| **Splash System** | Oil splashed by dipper | Motorbikes |
| **Pressure Feed System** | Oil pump delivers | Car engines |
| **Dry Sump System** | Separate oil tank | Aircraft engines |

**Functions:**  
Reduce wear, remove heat, clean surfaces, prevent corrosion.

---

## **17. Fuels and Combustion Quality**

| Property | Petrol Engine | Diesel Engine |
|-------------|----------------|----------------|
| **Rating** | Octane Number | Cetane Number |
| **Knock Resistance** | High octane â†’ less knock | High cetane â†’ better ignition |
| **Typical Rating** | 80â€“100 | 45â€“55 |

---

## **18. Engine Emissions and Control**

| Pollutant | Source | Control Method |
|-------------|-----------|----------------|
| **CO (Carbon Monoxide)** | Incomplete combustion | Proper mixture ratio |
| **NOx (Nitrogen Oxides)** | High temp | EGR, Catalytic converter |
| **HC (Hydrocarbons)** | Unburned fuel | Improved ignition |
| **Particulates** | Diesel soot | Filters |

**Emission Standards:** EURO, BS, EPA norms

---

## **19. Modern Engine Developments**

- **MPFI (Multi-Point Fuel Injection)** â†’ Precise fuel metering  
- **CRDi (Common Rail Direct Injection)** â†’ High-pressure diesel injection  
- **VVT (Variable Valve Timing)** â†’ Optimized efficiency  
- **Hybrid Systems** â†’ Combine IC + Electric motors  
- **Alternative Fuels:** LPG, CNG, Hydrogen, Biofuel  

---

> Thermodynamic Principles, Combustion Chemistry, Mechanical Design á€á€­á€¯á€·á€€á€­á€¯ á€¡á€á€¼á€±á€á€¶á€‘á€¬á€¸á€á€²á€·  
> Multi-disciplinary Engineering System á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

**á€¡á€€á€»á€‰á€ºá€¸á€á€»á€¯á€•á€º:**
> â€œFrom Ottoâ€™s spark to Dieselâ€™s compression â€”  
> the internal combustion engine remains a masterpiece of energy conversion,  
> evolving through innovation toward cleaner and more efficient technology.â€
