# â„ï¸ Chapter 13 â€“ Refrigeration and Air Conditioning  
*(Vapour Compression, Absorption, Psychrometry, Comfort Cooling Systems)*

---

## **Overview**

Refrigeration á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
á€á€…á€ºá€”á€±á€›á€¬á€€á€”á€± á€¡á€•á€°á€€á€­á€¯ á€–á€šá€ºá€›á€¾á€¬á€¸á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
á€¡á€á€¼á€¬á€¸á€”á€±á€›á€¬á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€á€­á€¯á€· á€œá€¾á€™á€ºá€¸á€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€· process á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  

> â€œRefrigeration is the process of removing heat from a low-temperature region and transferring it to a high-temperature region.â€

Air Conditioning á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ Refrigeration concept á€•á€±á€«á€ºá€™á€¾á€¬ á€¡á€á€¼á€±á€á€¶á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Temperature, Humidity, Air purity, Air motion á€€á€­á€¯ control á€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€· á€…á€”á€…á€º á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **1. Unit of Refrigeration**

**Ton of Refrigeration (TR):**

> 1 TR = Heat removed to freeze 1 ton (1000 kg) of water at 0Â°C in 24 hours.



1 TR = 211 kJ/min = 3.517 kW = 12,000 Btu/hr


---

## **2. Coefficient of Performance (COP)**

> Efficiency measure for refrigeration system.



COP = Q_L / W


Where:
- Q_L = Refrigeration effect (heat removed)
- W = Work input  

**Also:**


COP = T_L / (T_H - T_L)


Higher COP â†’ More efficient system.

---

## **3. Reverse Carnot Cycle**

> Theoretical maximum efficiency refrigeration cycle.

### **Processes:**
1. **1â€“2:** Isentropic compression  
2. **2â€“3:** Isothermal heat rejection (condenser)  
3. **3â€“4:** Isentropic expansion  
4. **4â€“1:** Isothermal heat absorption (evaporator)  

**COP (Carnot):**


COP = T_L / (T_H - T_L)


**Limitation:**  
Not practical due to non-isothermal compression and expansion.

---

## **4. Vapour Compression Refrigeration System (VCRS)**

> Most common refrigeration system used worldwide.

---

### **Main Components:**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Compressor** | Compresses refrigerant vapour â†’ high pressure |
| **Condenser** | Rejects heat to surroundings â†’ vapour â†’ liquid |
| **Expansion Valve** | Reduces pressure â†’ liquid partially evaporates |
| **Evaporator** | Absorbs heat â†’ cooling effect |

---

### **Cycle Description:**

1. **Evaporation:** Refrigerant absorbs heat from space â†’ vaporizes.  
2. **Compression:** Vapour compressed â†’ temperature rises.  
3. **Condensation:** Vapour condensed to liquid â†’ heat rejected.  
4. **Expansion:** Liquid throttled â†’ low pressure, low temp mixture formed.

---

### **Pâ€“h Diagram (Pressure vs Enthalpy)**


    |           .
    |      .  Condenser
    |  .            
    |.     .
    |       .
    |        . Expansion
    -------------------------
       Evaporator      Compressor


---

### **Work and COP:**



W = hâ‚‚ - hâ‚
Q_L = hâ‚ - hâ‚„
COP = (hâ‚ - hâ‚„) / (hâ‚‚ - hâ‚)


Where h = enthalpy (kJ/kg)

---

## **5. Vapour Absorption Refrigeration System (VARS)**

> Uses heat energy instead of mechanical work for compression.

---

### **Main Components:**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Generator** | Heat supplied â†’ refrigerant vapour separated |
| **Condenser** | Vapour â†’ liquid |
| **Evaporator** | Produces cooling effect |
| **Absorber** | Absorbs refrigerant vapour into absorbent solution |
| **Pump** | Circulates solution |

**Working Pair:**  
Ammoniaâ€“Water (NHâ‚ƒâ€“Hâ‚‚O) or Waterâ€“Lithium Bromide (Hâ‚‚Oâ€“LiBr)

---

### **Advantages of VARS:**
- No moving parts â†’ quiet operation  
- Uses waste heat / solar heat  
- Suitable for large-capacity systems  

**Disadvantages:**
- Low COP (~0.6â€“0.8)  
- Large equipment size  

---

## **6. Refrigerants**

> Substances used to absorb and reject heat during the refrigeration cycle.

---

### **Desirable Properties:**

| Property | Requirement |
|------------|---------------|
| **Thermodynamic** | High latent heat, low boiling point |
| **Physical** | Non-corrosive, non-toxic |
| **Chemical** | Stable, non-flammable |
| **Environmental** | Low ODP (Ozone Depletion Potential), Low GWP (Global Warming Potential) |

---

### **Common Refrigerants:**

| Refrigerant | Chemical Name | Application | Remarks |
|---------------|----------------|----------------|--------------|
| **R-12 (CClâ‚‚Fâ‚‚)** | Dichlorodifluoromethane | Domestic | Phased out (CFC) |
| **R-22 (CHClFâ‚‚)** | Chlorodifluoromethane | AC, Refrigeration | HCFC (phased down) |
| **R-134a (Câ‚‚Hâ‚‚Fâ‚„)** | Tetrafluoroethane | Car AC | HFC, zero ODP |
| **R-717 (NHâ‚ƒ)** | Ammonia | Industrial | Toxic but efficient |
| **R-600a (Câ‚„Hâ‚â‚€)** | Isobutane | Domestic | Eco-friendly |
| **R-290 (Câ‚ƒHâ‚ˆ)** | Propane | Modern chillers | Natural refrigerant |

---

## **7. Air Refrigeration System**

> Uses air as refrigerant (based on reverse Brayton or Bell-Coleman cycle).

**Used in:** Aircraft cooling systems.

**COP (Air refrigeration):**


COP = Tâ‚„ / (Tâ‚‚ - Tâ‚ƒ)


**Advantages:**
- Simple, lightweight  
**Disadvantages:**
- Low efficiency  

---

## **8. Refrigeration System Components (Detailed)**

### **Compressor:**
- Types: Reciprocating, Rotary, Scroll, Centrifugal  
- Function: Raise pressure & temperature of refrigerant vapour.

### **Condenser:**
- Rejects heat to cooling medium (air/water).  
- Types: Air-cooled, Water-cooled, Evaporative.

### **Expansion Device:**
- Controls flow to evaporator; reduces pressure.  
- Types: Capillary tube, Thermostatic Expansion Valve (TXV).

### **Evaporator:**
- Absorbs heat from space â†’ refrigerant vaporizes.  
- Types: Bare tube, Finned tube, Shell & Tube.

---

## **9. Psychrometry (Air Properties)**

> Study of moist air and its thermodynamic properties.

**Basic Terms:**

| Term | Symbol | Definition |
|--------|-----------|-------------|
| **Dry Bulb Temp (DBT)** | T_db | Ordinary air temperature |
| **Wet Bulb Temp (WBT)** | T_wb | Temp indicated by wet thermometer |
| **Dew Point Temp (DPT)** | T_dp | Temp at which condensation begins |
| **Humidity Ratio (w)** | â€” | Mass of water vapour / Mass of dry air |
| **Relative Humidity (RH)** | â€” | (Actual vapour pressure / Saturation vapour pressure) Ã— 100 |
| **Specific Humidity** | â€” | Similar to humidity ratio |
| **Enthalpy (h)** | kJ/kg | Total heat content of moist air |

---

### **Psychrometric Chart**

- X-axis â†’ Dry bulb temperature  
- Y-axis â†’ Humidity ratio  
- Curved line â†’ 100% saturation  
- Constant enthalpy, constant RH lines shown

**Used to analyze:**  
Cooling, heating, humidification, dehumidification processes.

---

## **10. Air Conditioning (A/C) System**

> Process of controlling temperature, humidity, purity, and motion of air.

---

### **Classification:**

| Type | Purpose | Example |
|--------|------------|------------|
| **Comfort A/C** | Human comfort | Offices, homes |
| **Industrial A/C** | Process stability | Textile, pharma |
| **Precision A/C** | Equipment control | Server rooms |

---

### **Basic Components:**

1. **Compressor** â€“ circulates refrigerant  
2. **Condenser** â€“ heat rejection  
3. **Expansion valve** â€“ throttling  
4. **Evaporator** â€“ cooling coil  
5. **Blower fan** â€“ air circulation  
6. **Filter** â€“ dust removal  

---

## **11. Cooling Load Components**

| Load Type | Description |
|-------------|---------------|
| **Sensible Heat Load** | Due to temperature difference |
| **Latent Heat Load** | Due to moisture removal |
| **Internal Load** | People, lights, machines |
| **External Load** | Walls, roof, windows |

---

### **Cooling Load Equation:**


Q_total = Q_sensible + Q_latent


---

## **12. Comfort Conditions**

> Standard indoor design for human comfort.

| Parameter | Typical Range |
|-------------|----------------|
| Temperature | 22â€“25Â°C |
| Relative Humidity | 40â€“60% |
| Air velocity | 0.15â€“0.25 m/s |
| Mean Radiant Temp | â‰ˆ Room temp |

**ASHRAE Comfort Zone:** 21â€“27Â°C and 40â€“60% RH.

---

## **13. Air Conditioning Processes**

| Process | On Psychrometric Chart | Effect |
|------------|-----------------------------|----------|
| **Sensible Cooling** | Horizontal left | â†“ DBT |
| **Dehumidification** | Left & down | â†“ DBT & â†“ humidity |
| **Evaporative Cooling** | Constant enthalpy | â†“ DBT, â†‘ RH |
| **Heating & Humidification** | Right & up | â†‘ DBT, â†‘ humidity |

---

## **14. Centralized A/C Systems**

| Type | Description | Application |
|--------|---------------|--------------|
| **All-Air System** | Conditioned air circulated | Large buildings |
| **All-Water System** | Chilled water loop | Hotels |
| **Airâ€“Water System** | Combined control | Hospitals |
| **Unitary System** | Packaged/Window unit | Small rooms |

## **15. Duct Design and Air Distribution**

> Ensures proper air delivery with minimal pressure loss.

**Key Concepts:**
- Velocity, friction loss, static pressure, total pressure  
- Duct materials: galvanized steel, aluminum, fiberglass  

**Design Methods:**
- Equal friction method  
- Static regain method  

---

## **16. Cooling Towers**

> Used to reject heat from condenser water to atmosphere.

**Types:**
- Natural draft (hyperbolic)  
- Forced draft (fan assisted)  

**Range:** T_hot â€“ T_cold  
**Approach:** T_cold â€“ T_wet bulb  

---

## **17. Performance of A/C System**

| Term | Formula | Description |
|--------|-----------|--------------|
| **COP** | Q_c / W | Efficiency |
| **EER (Energy Efficiency Ratio)** | (Cooling effect in Btu/hr) / Power input (W) | 1 TR = 12,000 Btu/hr |
| **SEER (Seasonal EER)** | Average over varying load | Modern metric |

---

- COâ‚‚ (R-744), Ammonia (R-717)  
- HFOs (R-1234yf)

**Green Refrigeration:**  
Use of natural refrigerants and renewable-powered systems.

# âš™ï¸ Chapter 14 â€“ Power Plant Engineering  
*(Steam, Hydro, Nuclear, Diesel, and Combined Cycle Power Plants)*

---

## **Overview**

Power Plant Engineering á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
Thermal Energy (á€¡á€•á€°á€¡á€„á€ºá€¡á€¬á€¸) á€€á€­á€¯ Electrical Energy (á€™á€®á€¸á€¡á€¬á€¸) á€¡á€–á€¼á€…á€º á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€·  
System á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á Design, Operation, Efficiency, Economics á€á€­á€¯á€·á€€á€­á€¯ á€œá€±á€·á€œá€¬á€á€Šá€·á€º subject á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

> â€œA power plant is an energy conversion system where primary energy sources are converted into useful electrical energy.â€

---

## **1. Types of Power Plants**

| Type | Energy Source | Working Medium |
|--------|----------------|----------------|
| **Thermal (Steam)** | Coal, Oil, Gas | Steam |
| **Hydro-Electric** | Water potential | Water |
| **Nuclear** | Atomic fission | Steam |
| **Diesel** | Diesel fuel | Combustion gas |
| **Gas Turbine** | Natural gas | Hot gases |
| **Combined Cycle** | Steam + Gas | Both |
| **Renewable** | Solar, Wind, Geothermal | Variable |

---

## **2. Thermal (Steam) Power Plant**

> Uses fossil fuel (coal) to produce steam that drives a turbine coupled to a generator.

---

### **Main Components:**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Boiler** | Converts water to high-pressure steam |
| **Superheater** | Raises steam temperature |
| **Turbine** | Converts steam energy to mechanical work |
| **Condenser** | Condenses exhaust steam to water |
| **Feed Pump** | Returns condensate to boiler |
| **Economiser** | Preheats feed water using flue gas |
| **Air Preheater** | Heats air before combustion |

---

### **Working Principle:**

1. Coal burned in furnace â†’ produces heat.  
2. Heat converts water into steam in the boiler.  
3. Steam expands in turbine â†’ produces mechanical work.  
4. Generator converts shaft work to electricity.  
5. Steam condensed in condenser â†’ reused by feed pump.

---

### **Rankine Cycle (Ideal Cycle):**

Processes:
1. **1â€“2:** Isentropic compression (pump)  
2. **2â€“3:** Constant pressure heat addition (boiler)  
3. **3â€“4:** Isentropic expansion (turbine)  
4. **4â€“1:** Constant pressure heat rejection (condenser)

**Thermal Efficiency:**


Î· = (hâ‚ƒ - hâ‚„) - (hâ‚‚ - hâ‚) / (hâ‚ƒ - hâ‚‚)


---

### **Improving Efficiency:**

- **Superheating:** Raises steam temperature  
- **Reheating:** Expands steam in stages  
- **Regeneration:** Heats feed water using turbine extraction steam  
- **Economiser & Air Preheater:** Recover waste heat  

---

## **3. Hydro-Electric Power Plant**

> Converts potential energy of water into mechanical and then electrical energy.

---

### **Main Components:**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Reservoir** | Stores water at height |
| **Penstock** | Pipe carrying water to turbine |
| **Turbine** | Converts kinetic energy â†’ mechanical |
| **Generator** | Converts mechanical â†’ electrical |
| **Tailrace** | Returns used water to river |

---

### **Types of Turbines:**

| Type | Head | Flow Direction | Example |
|--------|--------|------------------|------------|
| **Pelton Wheel** | High (>250 m) | Tangential | Mountain |
| **Francis Turbine** | Medium (30â€“250 m) | Mixed | Dams |
| **Kaplan Turbine** | Low (<30 m) | Axial | Run-of-river |

---

### **Advantages:**
- Renewable, clean, low running cost  
- Quick start-up  
- Long life (50â€“100 years)

**Disadvantages:**
- High initial cost  
- Site-dependent  
- Seasonal variation

---

## **4. Nuclear Power Plant**

> Uses controlled fission reaction to generate heat â†’ produce steam â†’ drive turbine.

---

### **Fission Reaction Example:**


UÂ²Â³âµ + n â†’ BaÂ¹â´Â¹ + Krâ¹Â² + 3n + 200 MeV


---

### **Main Components:**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Reactor** | Nuclear fission occurs, heat generated |
| **Moderator** | Slows down neutrons (Graphite, Heavy water) |
| **Control Rods** | Absorb excess neutrons (Cadmium, Boron) |
| **Coolant** | Transfers heat (COâ‚‚, Water, Sodium) |
| **Heat Exchanger** | Converts coolant heat â†’ steam |
| **Turbine & Generator** | Produce electricity |
| **Containment Vessel** | Ensures radiation safety |

---

### **Advantages:**
- High energy density  
- Low fuel cost  
- No greenhouse gases  

**Disadvantages:**
- Radioactive waste disposal  
- High capital cost  
- Safety concerns (meltdown risk)

---

### **Nuclear Reactors Types:**

| Reactor Type | Moderator | Coolant | Example |
|----------------|---------------|-------------|-------------|
| **PWR (Pressurised Water)** | Light water | Water | USA, France |
| **BWR (Boiling Water)** | Light water | Steam/water | Japan |
| **PHWR (Pressurised Heavy Water)** | Dâ‚‚O | Heavy water | India (CANDU) |
| **Fast Breeder Reactor** | None | Sodium | France, India |

---

## **5. Diesel Power Plant**

> Small-capacity power generation using diesel engine.

---

### **Main Components:**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Air Filter & Compressor** | Cleans and compresses air |
| **Fuel Injector** | Injects fuel into cylinder |
| **Engine (Cylinder)** | Converts chemical â†’ mechanical energy |
| **Cooling & Lubrication System** | Maintains temperature & reduces friction |
| **Alternator** | Converts mechanical â†’ electrical |
| **Exhaust System** | Removes gases |

---

### **Advantages:**
- Simple design, quick starting  
- Suitable for small load areas  
- Portable and reliable  

**Disadvantages:**
- High running cost  
- Noise and smoke  
- Limited capacity (<10 MW)

---

### **Applications:**
- Emergency standby  
- Remote area supply  
- Mobile units (ships, locomotives)

---

## **6. Gas Turbine Power Plant**

> Uses high-temperature, high-pressure gas to drive turbine directly.

---

### **Main Components:**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Compressor** | Compresses air |
| **Combustion Chamber** | Burns fuel â†’ hot gas |
| **Turbine** | Expands gas â†’ produces work |
| **Generator** | Produces electricity |

---

### **Brayton Cycle (Ideal Gas Turbine Cycle):**

1. **1â€“2:** Isentropic compression (compressor)  
2. **2â€“3:** Constant pressure heat addition (combustion)  
3. **3â€“4:** Isentropic expansion (turbine)  
4. **4â€“1:** Constant pressure heat rejection  

**Efficiency:**


Î· = 1 - (1 / r_p^((Î³-1)/Î³))


Where:
- r_p = Pressure ratio  
- Î³ = Cp/Cv  

---

### **Advantages:**
- Quick start, lightweight  
- Low maintenance  
- Uses multiple fuels (gas, kerosene)

**Disadvantages:**
- Low efficiency at part load  
- High-temperature materials required  

---

## **7. Combined Cycle Power Plant (CCPP)**

> Combines **Gas Turbine Cycle (Brayton)** + **Steam Cycle (Rankine)**  
for higher efficiency and energy recovery.

---

### **Working Principle:**

1. Gas turbine produces power â†’ hot exhaust (~500Â°C)  
2. Exhaust heat â†’ generates steam in **Heat Recovery Steam Generator (HRSG)**  
3. Steam drives steam turbine â†’ additional power  

**Overall Efficiency:**


Î·_total = Î·_gas + Î·_steam - (Î·_gas Ã— Î·_steam)
â‰ˆ 55â€“60%


---

### **Advantages:**
- High efficiency, low emissions  
- Compact, fast start-up  
- Fuel flexibility (natural gas, LNG)

**Disadvantages:**
- High initial cost  
- Complex system design  

---

## **8. Power Plant Performance**

| Parameter | Formula | Description |
|-------------|-----------|---------------|
| **Thermal Efficiency** | Î· = Output / Input | Efficiency of energy conversion |
| **Plant Load Factor (PLF)** | Actual output / Max possible output | Utilization level |
| **Plant Capacity Factor** | Average load / Rated capacity | Actual efficiency over time |
| **Plant Availability** | Running hours / Total hours | Reliability measure |
| **Heat Rate** | Energy input / Energy output | kJ/kWh |

---

## **9. Power Plant Economics**

| Cost Type | Description |
|-------------|--------------|
| **Fixed Cost** | Capital, maintenance, wages |
| **Running Cost** | Fuel, operation, consumables |
| **Depreciation** | Gradual loss of asset value |

**Tariff Design:**  
Block rate, two-part, flat rate, power factor tariff.

## **10. Environmental Impacts and Control**

| Source | Pollutant | Control Method |
|-----------|--------------|----------------|
| **Thermal** | COâ‚‚, SOâ‚‚, Fly ash | Electrostatic precipitator, scrubbers |
| **Diesel/Gas** | NOx, CO | Catalytic converter |
| **Nuclear** | Radiation | Shielding, containment |
| **Hydro** | Ecosystem disruption | Environmental design |

**Modern Focus:** Renewableâ€“Hybrid Power Integration.

---

## **11. Renewable & Hybrid Power Plants**

| Source | Technology | Remarks |
|----------|----------------|------------|
| **Solar Thermal** | Parabolic trough, tower | Heat â†’ Steam |
| **Solar PV** | Semiconductor cells | Direct electricity |
| **Wind** | Turbine blades | Clean energy |
| **Geothermal** | Underground steam | Constant source |
| **Hybrid (Solar + Thermal)** | Combined operation | Improved reliability |

## **12. Comparison of Power Plants**

| Type | Efficiency | Cost | Maintenance | Pollution | Suitability |
|--------|---------------|----------|----------------|---------------|----------------|
| **Thermal (Coal)** | 35â€“40% | Medium | Medium | High | Base load |
| **Hydro** | 85â€“90% | High initial | Low | Nil | Peak load |

| **Diesel** | 30â€“35% | Low | High | Moderate | Standby |
| **Gas Turbine** | 35â€“40% | Medium | Low | Low | Peak load |
| **Combined Cycle** | 55â€“60% | High | Medium | Low | Base load |

# ğŸŒ Chapter 15 â€“ Renewable Energy Systems  
*(Solar, Wind, Biomass, Geothermal, and Tidal Power)*

---

## **Overview**

Renewable Energy á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€á€˜á€¬á€á€¡á€› á€œá€Šá€ºá€•á€á€ºá€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€œá€Šá€ºá€á€­á€¯á€¸á€•á€½á€¬á€¸á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€²á€·  
á€¡á€„á€ºá€¡á€¬á€¸á€›á€„á€ºá€¸á€™á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€½á€±á€€á€­á€¯ á€†á€­á€¯á€œá€­á€¯á€á€¬á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  

> â€œRenewable energy is energy derived from natural processes that are replenished constantly â€” such as sunlight, wind, rain, tides, and geothermal heat.â€

Traditional fossil fuels á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€”á€²á€· á€”á€¾á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€¸á€šá€¾á€‰á€ºá€œá€­á€¯á€€á€ºá€›á€„á€º  
á€‘á€¯á€á€ºá€œá€½á€¾á€á€ºá€á€±á€¬ COâ‚‚ á€¡á€”á€Šá€ºá€¸á€†á€¯á€¶á€¸ á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Sustainable Development á€¡á€á€½á€€á€º á€¡á€á€¼á€±á€á€¶á€¡á€„á€ºá€¡á€¬á€¸á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

## **1. Classification of Energy Sources**

| Type | Description | Example |
|--------|---------------|------------|
| **Non-Renewable** | Finite sources | Coal, Oil, Gas |
| **Renewable** | Naturally replenished | Solar, Wind, Hydro |
| **Conventional** | Used traditionally | Hydro, Thermal |
| **Non-Conventional** | Newer technologies | Solar, Biomass, Tidal |

---

## **2. Solar Energy**

> Solar Energy á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€™á€¼á€”á€ºá€™á€¬á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€„á€¶á€œá€­á€¯ á€¡á€•á€°á€’á€á€ºá€™á€¼á€„á€·á€ºá€’á€±á€á€á€½á€±á€¡á€á€½á€€á€º á€¡á€›á€±á€¸á€€á€¼á€®á€¸á€†á€¯á€¶á€¸ Renewable Source á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

### **Solar Constant:**
> The amount of solar energy incident per unit area outside the Earth's atmosphere.



Solar constant = 1367 W/mÂ²


---

### **Solar Radiation Types:**
- **Direct (Beam) Radiation:** Comes straight from the sun.  
- **Diffuse Radiation:** Scattered by clouds/dust.  
- **Global Radiation:** Sum of both.

---

### **Solar Energy Utilization:**

| Type | System | Description |
|--------|-----------|---------------|
| **Thermal Conversion** | Solar collectors | Converts heat â†’ usable energy |
| **Photovoltaic Conversion (PV)** | Solar cells | Converts light â†’ electricity |

---

### **(a) Solar Thermal Systems**

| Type | Working Principle | Use |
|--------|--------------------|--------|
| **Flat Plate Collector** | Absorbs solar radiation on flat surface | Water heating |
| **Parabolic Trough Collector** | Focuses sunlight on receiver tube | Power generation |
| **Solar Tower** | Mirrors (heliostats) reflect to central receiver | High-temp process heat |

**Applications:**  
Water heating, cooking, desalination, power plants.

---

### **(b) Solar Photovoltaic (PV) System**

> Converts sunlight directly into DC electricity using semiconductor materials (Silicon).

**Basic Equation:**


P = V Ã— I


**Components:**
- **Solar Panel**
- **Charge Controller**
- **Battery**
- **Inverter**

**Efficiency:** 15â€“22%

**Applications:**  
Rural electrification, street lights, calculators, satellites.

---

## **3. Wind Energy**

> Converts kinetic energy of moving air into mechanical and electrical energy.

---

### **Power in Wind:**


P = Â½ Ï A VÂ³

Where:
- Ï = air density (kg/mÂ³)  
- A = swept area (Ï€rÂ²)  
- V = wind velocity (m/s)

---

### **Main Components of Wind Turbine:**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Rotor Blades** | Capture wind energy |
| **Hub & Shaft** | Transfer mechanical power |
| **Gearbox** | Increases rotational speed |
| **Generator** | Converts mechanical â†’ electrical |
| **Yaw System** | Faces turbine into wind |
| **Tower** | Provides height for wind capture |

---

### **Types of Wind Turbines:**

| Type | Axis | Example |
|--------|----------|-----------|
| **Horizontal Axis (HAWT)** | Horizontal | Most common |
| **Vertical Axis (VAWT)** | Vertical | Savonius, Darrieus |

---

### **Advantages:**
- Clean and renewable  
- Low operating cost  

**Disadvantages:**
- Intermittent supply  
- Noise, visual impact  

---

### **Applications:**
- Grid-connected farms  
- Remote microgrids  
- Water pumping systems  

---

## **4. Biomass Energy**

> Energy obtained from organic materials â€” plants, agricultural waste, animal manure, etc.

---

### **Biomass Conversion Methods:**

| Method | Process | Output |
|----------|-------------|-------------|
| **Combustion** | Direct burning | Heat, electricity |
| **Gasification** | Partial oxidation | Producer gas (CO + Hâ‚‚) |
| **Pyrolysis** | Thermal decomposition | Bio-oil, gas, char |
| **Anaerobic Digestion** | Microbial process | Biogas (CHâ‚„ + COâ‚‚) |

---

### **Biogas Plant:**

**Main Components:**
- Digester (air-tight tank)
- Inlet & outlet chambers
- Gas storage dome

**Equation:**


Câ‚†Hâ‚â‚‚Oâ‚† â†’ 3COâ‚‚ + 3CHâ‚„


**Uses:** Cooking, lighting, power generation.

---

### **Advantages:**
- Waste utilization  
- Carbon neutral  
- Continuous supply  

**Limitations:**
- Large land required  
- Low energy density  

---

## **5. Geothermal Energy**

> Heat energy extracted from the Earthâ€™s interior.

---

### **Types of Geothermal Resources:**

| Type | Source | Temperature (Â°C) | Example |
|--------|------------|----------------|-------------|
| **Dry Steam** | Steam directly | >250Â°C | Geysers (USA) |
| **Wet Steam / Flash Steam** | Hot water + steam | 180â€“250Â°C | Italy, Philippines |
| **Hot Water (Binary Cycle)** | Moderate water | 100â€“180Â°C | Iceland |

---

### **Working Principle:**
1. Hot water/steam extracted from underground reservoir.  
2. Steam drives turbine â†’ generates electricity.  
3. Condensed water re-injected â†’ sustainability.

---

### **Advantages:**
- Reliable base load power  
- Low emissions  
- Small land footprint  

**Disadvantages:**
- Site-specific  
- Risk of depletion and scaling  

---

## **6. Tidal and Wave Energy**

> Harnessing energy from ocean movements (tides and waves).

---

### **(a) Tidal Energy**

**Principle:**  
Energy due to periodic rise and fall of seawater levels (gravitational pull of moon and sun).

**Power Equation:**


P = Â½ Ï g A hÂ²

Where h = tidal range.

**System Types:**
- Tidal barrage (dam type)
- Tidal stream turbines

**Sites:** France (La Rance), UK, South Korea

---

### **(b) Wave Energy**

> Energy from surface waves caused by wind.

**Devices:**
- Oscillating Water Column (OWC)  
- Floating Buoys  
- Wave Overtopping Device  

**Applications:**  
Coastal power, desalination, hydrogen generation.

---

## **7. Ocean Thermal Energy Conversion (OTEC)**

> Uses temperature difference between warm surface water and cold deep water to generate power.

**Working Principle:**
- Warm water evaporates working fluid (ammonia).  
- Vapour drives turbine â†’ condenser cooled by cold seawater.

**Efficiency:** 2â€“3% (small but continuous).

**Major Sites:** India (NIO), Hawaii, Japan.

---

## **8. Hydrogen Energy**

> Future fuel â€” clean and high energy density.

**Production Methods:**
- Electrolysis of water  
- Steam reforming of natural gas  
- Biomass gasification  

**Uses:**
- Fuel cells, rockets, hybrid vehicles.

**Advantages:**  
Zero emission (Hâ‚‚ + Oâ‚‚ â†’ Hâ‚‚O + energy)

---

## **9. Energy Storage Systems**

| Type | Example | Purpose |
|--------|------------|-----------|
| **Mechanical** | Flywheel, Pumped hydro | Short-term backup |
| **Electrical** | Supercapacitor | Instant response |
| **Electrochemical** | Batteries (Li-ion, Na-ion) | Grid storage |
| **Thermal** | Molten salt, Ice | Store solar heat |

**Importance:** Balances intermittent renewable sources.

---

## **10. Hybrid Renewable Systems**

> Combine multiple renewable sources for reliability.

| Combination | Application |
|----------------|------------------|
| Solar + Wind | Rural microgrids |
| Solar + Biomass | Industrial |
| Wind + Diesel | Island systems |
| PV + Battery + Grid | Smart homes |

**Advantage:**  
Stable supply, better utilization, load balancing.

---

## **11. Environmental Benefits**

| Aspect | Impact |
|-----------|-------------|
| **Air Quality** | Zero emissions |
| **Climate Change** | Reduces COâ‚‚ footprint |
| **Water Use** | Minimal compared to thermal plants |
| **Waste** | Utilizes organic residues |

---

## **12. Limitations of Renewable Energy**

- Intermittent supply (solar/wind)  
- High initial investment  
- Land and storage requirements  
- Transmission and grid integration challenges  

---

## **13. Global and Myanmar Scenario**

| Source | Global Trend | Myanmar Status |
|-----------|------------------|----------------|
| **Solar** | Rapid growth (China, India) | Pilot projects (Mandalay, Minbu) |
| **Hydro** | Mature technology | Major contributor (Yeywa, Myitsone sites) |
| **Wind** | Expanding | Early-stage feasibility studies |
| **Biomass** | Rural potential | Rice husk, wood waste use |
| **Geothermal** | Niche | Exploration ongoing (Tachileik, Shan State) |

**Myanmar Potential:**  
> With over 300 sunny days annually and extensive river systems, the country has vast renewable potential for decentralized power generation.

---

## **14. Future of Renewable Energy**

- Smart grids & microgrids  
- AI-based energy management  
- Floating solar farms  
- Offshore wind  
- Hydrogen integration

# ğŸš† Chapter 16 â€“ Electric Drives and Traction  
*(DC/AC Drives, Control Systems, Electric Vehicles, and Railway Traction)*

---

## **Overview**

**Electric Drive** á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
Electric Motor á€€á€­á€¯ Mechanical Load á€”á€²á€· á€‘á€­á€”á€ºá€¸á€á€»á€¯á€•á€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸ á€œá€Šá€ºá€•á€á€ºá€¡á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€·  
System á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  

> â€œAn Electric Drive is an arrangement which controls the speed, torque, and direction of an electric motor to perform mechanical work efficiently.â€

Power Electronics, Control Theory, and Motor Technology  
á€á€½á€±á€€á€­á€¯ á€•á€±á€«á€„á€ºá€¸á€…á€•á€ºá€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€á€²á€· Applied Engineering field á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€•á€²á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

## **1. Elements of an Electric Drive System**

| Component | Function |
|-------------|-------------|
| **Power Source** | Supplies electrical energy (AC/DC) |
| **Power Modulator (Converter/Inverter)** | Controls voltage, current, frequency |
| **Motor** | Converts electrical â†’ mechanical energy |
| **Load** | Performs mechanical work |
| **Control Unit** | Maintains speed/torque as required |
| **Sensors/Feedback** | Measure variables (speed, current, position) |

**Control Loop:**  
Power Supply â†’ Converter â†’ Motor â†’ Load â†’ Sensor Feedback â†’ Controller

---

## **2. Types of Electric Drives**

| Type | Supply | Motor Type |
|--------|-----------|--------------|
| **DC Drives** | DC Supply | DC Motor |
| **AC Drives** | AC Supply | Induction, Synchronous Motor |
| **Stepper/Servo Drives** | Controlled Supply | Stepper, Servo Motor |
| **Hybrid Drives** | AC + DC | Mixed systems |

---

## **3. Advantages of Electric Drives**

- High efficiency  
- Easy control of speed and torque  
- Clean and quiet operation  
- Automatic protection and feedback  
- Flexible for industrial automation  

---

## **4. DC Motor Drives**

> DC Drives are widely used for precise speed and torque control.

---

### **Speed Equation:**


N âˆ (V - IaRa) / Î¦

Where:  
N = speed, V = supply voltage, Ia = armature current, Ra = armature resistance, Î¦ = flux.

---

### **Speed Control Methods:**

| Method | Control | Used in |
|-----------|------------|-----------|
| **Armature Voltage Control** | Below rated speed | Constant torque |
| **Field Weakening** | Above rated speed | Constant power |
| **Armature Resistance Control** | Series resistor | Simple, inefficient |

---

### **DC Motor Types:**
- **DC Shunt Motor:** Constant speed  
- **DC Series Motor:** High starting torque (Traction use)  
- **DC Compound Motor:** Combination of both

---

## **5. AC Motor Drives**

> AC Drives use power electronic converters (Inverters) to control voltage and frequency.

---

### **Types:**

| Drive Type | Motor | Converter Used |
|----------------|-------------|----------------|
| **V/f Control Drive** | Induction Motor | Inverter |
| **Vector Control Drive (Field Oriented Control)** | Induction/Synchronous | PWM Inverter + DSP |
| **Direct Torque Control (DTC)** | Induction | Advanced control |
| **Synchronous Motor Drive** | Permanent Magnet | VSC (Voltage Source Converter) |

---

### **V/f Control Principle:**
> Maintain constant magnetic flux by keeping the ratio of voltage to frequency constant.



V / f = constant


---

### **Advantages of AC Drives:**
- Maintenance-free  
- Suitable for variable speed  
- High efficiency & precise control  

---

## **6. Power Electronic Converters in Drives**

| Converter | Type | Function |
|--------------|-----------|-------------|
| **Rectifier** | AC â†’ DC | Used in DC drives |
| **Chopper** | DC â†’ variable DC | Speed control |
| **Inverter** | DC â†’ AC | AC drive control |
| **Cycloconverter** | AC â†’ variable AC | Low-speed large motor control |

---

### **PWM (Pulse Width Modulation)**

> Technique to control output voltage of inverter by varying pulse width while keeping frequency constant.

Advantages:
- Smooth control  
- Low harmonic distortion  
- High dynamic response  

---

## **7. Torque-Speed Characteristics**

**Quadrant Operation:**

| Quadrant | Mode | Description |
|--------------|--------|----------------|
| I | Forward Motoring | Driving in forward direction |
| II | Forward Braking | Regenerative braking |
| III | Reverse Motoring | Reverse direction |
| IV | Reverse Braking | Braking in reverse |

Drives capable of all 4 quadrants â†’ **Four-Quadrant Drives**

---

## **8. Regenerative Braking**

> Converts kinetic energy of motor/load into electrical energy and returns it to the supply.

**Used in:**  
Electric vehicles, cranes, elevators, trains.

**Advantages:**
- Energy saving  
- Less mechanical wear  

---

## **9. Electric Traction Systems**

> The system that uses electrical energy to propel vehicles like trains, trams, or metro systems.

---

### **Traction Supply Systems:**

| Type | Supply Voltage | Application |
|--------|------------------|----------------|
| **DC Traction** | 600 V, 1500 V, 3000 V | Trams, Metro |
| **AC Traction (Single Phase)** | 15â€“25 kV, 50 Hz | Mainline Railways |
| **Three Phase AC** | 3.3â€“6.6 kV | Industrial Railways |

---

### **DC vs AC Traction Comparison**

| Parameter | DC System | AC System |
|--------------|--------------|--------------|
| Voltage | Low | High |
| Substations | Many | Few |
| Maintenance | High | Low |
| Losses | High | Low |
| Application | Metro, urban | Mainline, long routes |

---

## **10. Traction Motors**

| Motor Type | Feature | Used In |
|---------------|--------------|--------------|
| **DC Series Motor** | High starting torque | Trains, trams |
| **AC Induction Motor** | Robust, low maintenance | Modern locomotives |
| **Permanent Magnet Motor** | Compact, efficient | Electric Vehicles |
| **Synchronous Motor** | High-speed trains | Bullet trains |

---

## **11. Braking in Electric Traction**

| Type | Description |
|-----------|----------------|
| **Regenerative Braking** | Returns energy to line |
| **Dynamic Braking** | Energy dissipated in resistor |
| **Plugging** | Reverse current applied for quick stop |
| **Mechanical Braking** | Friction-based, auxiliary only |

---

## **12. Speed-Time Curve (Train Dynamics)**

> Used for analyzing performance of traction system.

### **Phases:**
1. **Acceleration** â€“ Starting torque high  
2. **Constant Speed** â€“ Cruising phase  
3. **Coasting** â€“ Power off, inertia runs  
4. **Braking** â€“ Stopping phase  

**Key Parameters:**
- Average speed  
- Schedule speed  
- Specific energy consumption  

---

## **13. Electric Vehicle (EV) Drives**

> Application of electric drives in transportation (cars, buses, scooters, trains).

---

### **Components of EV Drive System:**

| Component | Function |
|--------------|--------------|
| **Battery Pack** | Energy storage |
| **Inverter/Converter** | Power conditioning |
| **Motor** | Propulsion |
| **Controller** | Speed/torque management |
| **Regenerative Braking System** | Energy recovery |

---

### **Motor Types for EVs:**

| Type | Feature | Example |
|--------|-------------|------------|
| **BLDC Motor (Brushless DC)** | High efficiency, compact | E-bikes |
| **Induction Motor** | Rugged, cheap | Tesla Model S |
| **Permanent Magnet Synchronous Motor (PMSM)** | High torque density | Modern EVs |
| **Switched Reluctance Motor (SRM)** | Robust, simple | Industrial EVs |

---

### **EV Drive Control:**

- **PWM Inverter** for torque control  
- **Vector Control / DTC** for high performance  
- **Battery Management System (BMS)** monitors voltage, temperature, SOC  

---

### **EV Charging Methods:**

| Type | Voltage | Description |
|--------|------------|----------------|
| **Level 1** | 120V AC | Slow (home) |
| **Level 2** | 240V AC | Medium (public) |
| **DC Fast Charging** | 400â€“800V DC | Rapid charging |
| **Wireless Charging** | Inductive | Emerging tech |

---

## **14. Control of Electric Drives**

### **Open Loop Control**
- No feedback  
- Simple but less accurate  

### **Closed Loop Control**
- Feedback from sensors (speed, current, torque)  
- PID or microcontroller-based control  

**Modern Drives Use:**  
Digital control (DSP, PLC, Microcontrollers)

---

## **15. Safety and Protection Systems**

| Fault | Protection Device |
|-----------|----------------------|
| Overcurrent | Fuse, Circuit breaker |
| Overvoltage | Surge absorber |
| Overtemperature | Thermal relay |
| Ground fault | Differential protection |
| Stall condition | Automatic cut-off |

---

## **16. Recent Trends in Electric Drives**

- Smart sensor-based monitoring  
- IoT-enabled predictive maintenance  
- Regenerative braking integration  
- High-speed traction using SiC-based inverters  
- EVâ€“Grid integration (Vehicle-to-Grid, V2G)

---

## **17. Advantages of Electric Traction**

- Smooth and fast acceleration  
- Less maintenance  
- High efficiency and regenerative braking  
- Environmentally clean  

**Disadvantages:**
- High capital cost  
- Dependence on power supply network  

---

## **18. Applications of Electric Drives**

| Application | Drive Used |
|----------------|----------------|
| Steel mills | DC/AC Variable Speed Drives |
| Cement plants | Induction motor drives |
| Electric trains | DC series / AC induction drives |
| Cranes & elevators | DC/AC regenerative drives |
| Electric vehicles | PMSM / BLDC drives |

---

## **19. Future of Electric Mobility**

- Integration with renewable energy  
- Smart grid & wireless charging  
- Solid-state batteries  
- Autonomous EV control drives  
- AI-based efficiency optimization  

---

# âš¡ Chapter 17 â€“ Power Electronics Applications  
*(Converters, Inverters, Choppers, and Industrial Control Systems)*

---

## **Overview**

**Power Electronics** á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
Electrical Power á€€á€­á€¯ Electronic Devices á€á€½á€±á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Control, Convert, Condition á€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€· Engineering Field á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  

> â€œPower Electronics bridges the gap between electrical energy and electronic control â€” enabling efficient conversion and regulation of power for all modern applications.â€

---

## **1. Introduction to Power Electronics**

Power Electronics System á€á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€™á€¾á€¬  
Power Semiconductor Devices (like SCR, MOSFET, IGBT) á€€á€­á€¯ á€¡á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€•á€¼á€¯á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
AC â†” DC â†” AC â†” Variable Power á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€¡á€±á€¬á€„á€º á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€•á€±á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

**Main Function:**  
- Convert (ACâ†”DCâ†”AC)  
- Control voltage/current/frequency  
- Regulate power flow  

---

## **2. Basic Power Electronic Converters**

| Converter Type | Conversion | Example |
|-------------------|----------------|------------|
| **Rectifier** | AC â†’ DC | Power supply |
| **Inverter** | DC â†’ AC | Motor drives |
| **Chopper** | DC â†’ variable DC | Speed control |
| **Cycloconverter** | AC â†’ variable AC | Low-speed drive |
| **AC Voltage Controller** | AC â†’ Controlled AC | Dimmers, heaters |

---

## **3. Power Semiconductor Devices**

| Device | Type | Key Feature |
|-----------|----------|----------------|
| **Diode** | Uncontrolled | One-way current flow |
| **Thyristor (SCR)** | Semi-controlled | Triggered by gate |
| **Triac** | AC control | Bidirectional conduction |
| **GTO (Gate Turn-Off Thyristor)** | Fully controlled | Turn off via gate |
| **BJT / MOSFET** | Fast switching | Low/medium power |
| **IGBT** | Hybrid (BJT+MOSFET) | High efficiency, high power |

---

### **Switching Characteristics**
- **Turn-on time**
- **Turn-off time**
- **Rise and fall times**
  
Fast switching â†’ Higher efficiency and compact design.

---

## **4. Rectifiers (AC to DC Converters)**

> Rectifier á€á€Šá€º Alternating Current (AC) á€€á€­á€¯ Direct Current (DC) á€á€­á€¯á€· á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€•á€±á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

---

### **Types of Rectifiers:**

| Type | Phase | Control | Example |
|--------|-----------|-------------|-------------|
| **Half-Wave Rectifier** | Single-phase | Uncontrolled | Simple circuits |
| **Full-Wave Rectifier** | Single-phase | Uncontrolled | Center-tap or bridge |
| **Three-Phase Rectifier** | Three-phase | Uncontrolled/Controlled | Industrial supply |
| **Controlled Rectifier (Using SCR)** | Single/3-phase | Fully controlled | DC motor drives |

---

### **Average DC Output Voltage (Single-Phase Full Converter):**


Vdc = (2Vm / Ï€) Ã— cos Î±

Where Î± = firing angle.

---

### **Applications:**
- DC motor control  
- Battery charging  
- HVDC transmission systems  

---

## **5. Choppers (DC-DC Converters)**

> Converts fixed DC voltage to variable DC voltage.

---

### **Principle:**
Switch ON/OFF rapidly using transistor or MOSFET.

**Output Voltage:**


Vout = D Ã— Vin

Where D = Duty cycle (Ton / (Ton + Toff))

---

### **Types of Choppers:**

| Type | Operation | Example |
|--------|--------------|-------------|
| **Step-Down (Buck)** | Vout < Vin | DC motor control |
| **Step-Up (Boost)** | Vout > Vin | EV systems |
| **Buck-Boost** | Vout variable | Battery systems |
| **Cuk, SEPIC, Flyback** | Isolated control | Power supplies |

---

### **Applications:**
- DC motor speed control  
- Battery charging  
- DC voltage regulators  

---

## **6. Inverters (DC to AC Converters)**

> Converts DC power to AC with controlled frequency and amplitude.

---

### **Types of Inverters:**

| Type | Description | Application |
|--------|----------------|----------------|
| **Single-phase inverter** | 1Ï† output | Small loads |
| **Three-phase inverter** | 3Ï† balanced output | Industrial motors |
| **Voltage Source Inverter (VSI)** | Constant DC input | Induction drives |
| **Current Source Inverter (CSI)** | Constant current input | High-power drives |
| **PWM Inverter** | Pulse control | Variable speed control |

---

### **Output Voltage Control by PWM:**
Adjust pulse width â†’ Control RMS voltage and reduce harmonics.

**THD â†“ Efficiency â†‘**

---

### **Applications:**
- AC motor drives  
- UPS systems  
- Renewable energy systems (Solar PV, Wind)  

---

## **7. Cycloconverters (AC to AC)**

> Converts constant AC voltage at one frequency â†’ variable AC voltage at another (usually lower) frequency.

**Used for:**  
Low-speed, high-torque applications like rolling mills, cement kilns, and ship propulsion.

---

### **Advantages:**
- Direct AC control (no DC link)
- Smooth speed variation  

**Disadvantages:**
- Complex circuit  
- Low output frequency (< â…“ of input)

---

## **8. AC Voltage Controllers**

> Control RMS voltage of AC supply using phase control (Triac or SCR).

**Used in:**
- Lamp dimming  
- Induction heating  
- Domestic heaters  

**Average Voltage:**


Vavg = Vm(1 + cos Î±)/Ï€


---

## **9. Power Electronic Control in Motor Drives**

| Motor Type | Converter Used | Control |
|----------------|------------------|---------------|
| **DC Motor** | Controlled Rectifier / Chopper | Voltage / Field control |
| **AC Induction Motor** | Inverter | V/f or Vector control |
| **Stepper Motor** | Chopper Drive | Pulse control |
| **Servo Motor** | PWM Amplifier | Position / speed control |

---

## **10. Power Electronics in Industrial Automation**

> Modern industries use power electronic converters to precisely control process variables like torque, speed, and temperature.

**Applications:**
- **CNC Machines** â€“ Servo drives  
- **Robotics** â€“ BLDC control  
- **Elevators / Cranes** â€“ Regenerative drives  
- **Textile & Paper Mills** â€“ Variable frequency drives (VFDs)

---

### **Advantages:**
- Energy saving  
- Smooth operation  
- Reduced maintenance  
- Better process accuracy  

---

## **11. Power Electronics in Renewable Energy Systems**

| Source | Converter | Application |
|-----------|---------------|----------------|
| **Solar PV** | DC-DC Boost + Inverter | Grid-tied solar system |
| **Wind Turbine** | AC-DC-AC converter | Variable speed generation |
| **Fuel Cell** | DC-DC Converter | Hybrid vehicle supply |
| **Battery Storage** | Bidirectional converter | Charge/discharge control |

---

### **Smart Grid Integration:**
Power electronics manage **bidirectional power flow** between grid, renewable sources, and energy storage.

---

## **12. Power Electronics in Electric Vehicles (EVs)**

**Converter Systems in EVs:**
- DC-DC Chopper â†’ Battery voltage regulation  
- Inverter â†’ Motor drive control  
- Regenerative braking â†’ Energy recovery  

**Efficiency:** 90â€“95%  

**Control Algorithms:**  
FOC (Field Oriented Control), DTC (Direct Torque Control)

---

## **13. Power Factor Improvement**

> Power electronic circuits can cause low power factor (due to harmonics).  
To correct this, **Active Power Factor Correction (PFC)** circuits are used.

**Techniques:**
- Boost Converter PFC  
- Synchronous rectification  
- Digital control (DSP-based)  

---

## **14. Harmonics and Filters**

**Problem:** Non-linear loads â†’ Harmonics â†’ Distorted waveforms.

**Solution:**
- **Passive Filters (L-C)**
- **Active Filters (IGBT-based)**  
Used in UPS, HVDC, and industrial systems.

---

## **15. HVDC and FACTS Controllers**

| Technology | Function | Converter Type |
|---------------|----------------|----------------|
| **HVDC (High Voltage DC Transmission)** | Long-distance power transfer | Line-Commutated or VSC |
| **FACTS (Flexible AC Transmission Systems)** | Improve stability and control | STATCOM, SVC, UPFC |

**Modern Devices:** IGBT, GTO, IGCT  
**Benefit:** Efficient grid voltage and reactive power management.

---

## **16. Protection in Power Electronic Systems**

| Fault | Protection Device |
|-----------|----------------------|
| Overcurrent | Fuse, Fast-acting breaker |
| Overvoltage | Snubber, Surge suppressor |
| Short-circuit | Electronic protection |
| Thermal overload | Heat sink, cooling fan |
| Reverse polarity | Diode protection |

---

## **17. Thermal Management**

> Switching devices generate heat â†’ requires cooling for reliability.

**Cooling Methods:**
- Heat sinks  
- Forced air cooling  
- Liquid cooling  
- Thermal interface materials  

**IGBT junction temperature:** typically 125â€“150Â°C maximum.

---

## **18. Power Electronic Control Systems**

| Control Type | Description |
|------------------|----------------|
| **Analog Control** | Op-amp based PWM control |
| **Digital Control** | Microcontroller, DSP |
| **Feedback Control** | Uses sensors for closed-loop stability |

Modern converters use **Digital Signal Processors (DSPs)** for real-time control.

---

## **19. Emerging Applications**

- Smart home power management  
- Wireless charging (Inductive Power Transfer)  
- Solid-state transformers (SST)  
- Electric aircraft propulsion  
- Renewable-grid integration  

---

## **Overview**

**Electric Power Utilization** á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬  
á€‘á€¯á€á€ºá€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€‘á€¬á€¸á€á€²á€· á€œá€»á€¾á€•á€ºá€…á€…á€ºá€…á€½á€™á€ºá€¸á€¡á€„á€ºá€€á€­á€¯ á€¡á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€•á€¼á€¯á€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
á€¡á€‘á€°á€¸á€á€–á€¼á€„á€·á€º á€¡á€œá€„á€ºá€¸á€›á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸áŠ á€¡á€•á€°á€•á€±á€¸á€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸áŠ á€¡á€á€á€ºá€¡á€‘á€Šá€ºá€¡á€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€™á€»á€¬á€¸áŠ  
á€…á€€á€ºá€™á€¾á€¯á€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€„á€”á€ºá€¸á€™á€»á€¬á€¸á€á€½á€„á€º á€‘á€­á€›á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€¡á€±á€¬á€„á€º á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€…á€½á€²á€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸á€€á€­á€¯ á€†á€­á€¯á€œá€­á€¯á€á€šá€ºá‹  

> â€œElectric power utilization refers to the efficient and effective use of electrical energy for lighting, heating, welding, traction, and industrial purposes.â€

## **1. Introduction to Electric Power Utilization**

- Generation â†’ Transmission â†’ Distribution â†’ **Utilization**
- Objective: To convert electrical energy into useful forms like light, heat, and mechanical energy.
- Efficient utilization reduces energy waste and cost.

## **2. Electric Heating**

> Electric Heating á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ Electrical Energy á€€á€­á€¯ Heat Energy á€¡á€–á€¼á€…á€º á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€·á€”á€Šá€ºá€¸á€œá€™á€ºá€¸á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

**Advantages:**
- Clean (no combustion)
- Quick and controllable heating
- High efficiency (~90â€“95%)
- Uniform temperature
- Easy automation

---

### **Types of Electric Heating**

| Type | Principle | Example |
|--------|----------------|----------------|
| **Resistance Heating** | Jouleâ€™s Law (IÂ²R loss) | Electric oven, water heater |
| **Induction Heating** | Electromagnetic induction | Metal hardening, melting |
| **Dielectric Heating (RF Heating)** | Polar molecule vibration | Plastic welding, drying |
| **Arc Heating** | Electric arc temperature (~3500Â°C) | Arc furnaces |
| **Infrared Heating** | Radiant energy absorption | Paint drying, textile |

---

### **(a) Resistance Heating**

**Jouleâ€™s Law:**


H = IÂ² R t


**Applications:**
- Domestic heaters
- Toasters, irons
- Industrial ovens

**Materials:** Nichrome, Kanthal, Constantan

---

### **(b) Induction Heating**

> Heating due to **eddy currents** induced in the metal by alternating magnetic field.

**Applications:**
- Induction furnace (steel melting)
- Surface hardening of tools
- Cooking induction plates

---

### **(c) Dielectric Heating**

> Used for insulating materials (non-metals).

**Frequency range:** 10 MHz â€“ 50 MHz  
**Used in:** Plastic welding, wood gluing, textile drying

---

### **(d) Arc Heating**

> High temperature from electric arc between electrodes.

**Two types:**
- **Direct Arc:** Current flows through charge (e.g. steel furnace)
- **Indirect Arc:** Arc forms between electrodes only (e.g. laboratory furnaces)

---

## **3. Electric Welding**

> Electric Welding á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ Metal parts á€”á€¾á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€€á€­á€¯ Heat + Pressure á€–á€¼á€„á€·á€º á€¡á€á€°á€•á€±á€«á€„á€ºá€¸á€…á€Šá€ºá€¸á€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸ á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

### **Classification of Electric Welding**

| Type | Method | Application |
|---------|-------------|----------------|
| **Resistance Welding** | Heat by resistance (IÂ²R) | Sheet metal, auto body |
| **Arc Welding** | Heat by electric arc | Construction, pipelines |
| **Gas Welding (Oxy-acetylene)** | Combustion | Repairs |
| **Spot Welding** | Local heating between electrodes | Vehicle manufacturing |

---

### **(a) Resistance Welding**

**Principle:** Heat generated at joint due to contact resistance.



H = IÂ² R t


**Types:**
- Spot Welding  
- Seam Welding  
- Projection Welding  
- Butt Welding  

**Advantages:**
- Fast and clean  
- No filler material needed  
- Automation possible

---

### **(b) Arc Welding**

> Uses high-temperature electric arc (up to 3500Â°C) between electrode and workpiece.

**Power Supply:** AC or DC  
**Electrode:** Consumable / Non-consumable  
**Shielding:** Gas (COâ‚‚, Argon)

**Applications:**  
Bridges, ships, heavy steel structures.

---

## **4. Electric Lighting**

> Lighting is the most common form of electrical energy utilization for visibility, decoration, and productivity.

---

### **Luminous Terms**

| Term | Symbol | Unit | Description |
|---------|------------|-------------|----------------|
| **Luminous Flux** | Î¦ | Lumen (lm) | Light emitted per second |
| **Luminous Intensity** | I | Candela (cd) | Flux per unit solid angle |
| **Illuminance** | E | Lux (lm/mÂ²) | Light falling on surface |
| **Luminance** | L | cd/mÂ² | Brightness of surface |
| **Efficacy** | Î· | lm/W | Light output per power input |

---

### **Types of Electric Lamps**

| Type | Principle | Efficiency | Typical Use |
|----------|------------------|----------------|----------------|
| **Incandescent Lamp** | Filament heating | 10â€“15 lm/W | Domestic |
| **Fluorescent Lamp** | Gas discharge + phosphor coating | 50â€“100 lm/W | Offices |
| **Mercury Vapor Lamp** | UV discharge | 40â€“60 lm/W | Street lighting |
| **Sodium Vapor Lamp** | Na vapor emission | 100â€“150 lm/W | Highways |
| **LED Lamp (Light Emitting Diode)** | Semiconductor emission | 100â€“200 lm/W | All modern uses |

---

### **Advantages of LED Lighting**

- High luminous efficiency  
- Long life (50,000+ hours)  
- Low energy consumption  
- Eco-friendly (no mercury)  
- Instant start, dimmable  

---

### **Lighting Schemes**

| Scheme | Description | Example |
|-----------|----------------|----------------|
| **Direct Lighting** | 90â€“100% direct light | Office lights |
| **Semi-Direct** | 60â€“90% down, 10â€“40% up | Stores |
| **Indirect** | Reflected from ceiling | Theatres |
| **General Diffused** | Uniform lighting | Showrooms |

---

### **Street Lighting Systems**

| Type | Layout | Feature |
|---------|------------|-------------|
| **Series System** | Lamps in series | Simple but unsafe |
| **Parallel System** | Lamps in parallel | Safe, modern |
| **Group Control** | Controlled together | City lighting networks |

## **5. Energy Conservation**

> Energy Conservation á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬ á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€…á€½á€²á€™á€¾á€¯á€¡á€á€½á€€á€º á€‘á€­á€›á€±á€¬á€€á€ºá€¡á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸á€”á€²á€·

2. Load analysis  
3. Identify inefficiencies  
4. Recommend improvements  

**Benefits:**  
Cost saving, improved reliability, environmental protection.

## **6. Power Factor Improvement**

> Low power factor causes high current and losses. Improving it increases efficiency.

**Power Factor (pf):**


pf = cos Ï† = Active Power / Apparent Power


**Methods:**
- Use **Capacitor Banks**
- **Synchronous Condenser**
- **Phase Advancers**

**Benefits:**
- Reduced losses  
- Improved voltage regulation  
- Better utilization of equipment

## **7. Electric Drives in Utilization Systems**

|----------------|----------------|----------------|

| **Rolling Mills** | DC motor | Armature control |

## **8. Efficiency and Load Factor**

**Load Factor:**


Load Factor = Average Load / Maximum Load


**Higher load factor â†’ lower cost per kWh**

**Overall Efficiency:**


Î· = (Useful Output Power / Input Power) Ã— 100%


**To improve efficiency:**
- Avoid overloading  
- Regular maintenance  
- Use energy-efficient motors (IE3/IE4)  

---

## **9. Energy Storage and Demand Management**

- Load shifting

# âš™ï¸ Chapter 19 â€“ Smart Grid and Future Power Systems  
*(Automation, IoT, AI, and Renewable Energy Integration)*

---

## **Overview**

**Smart Grid** á€†á€­á€¯á€á€¬á€Ÿá€¬ á€œá€»á€¾á€•á€ºá€…á€…á€ºá€…á€”á€…á€ºá€¡á€”á€¬á€‚á€á€ºá€•á€¯á€¶á€…á€¶á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Digital Communication, Automation, IoT (Internet of Things), AI (Artificial Intelligence)  
á€”á€²á€· Renewable Energy á€€á€­á€¯ á€•á€±á€«á€„á€ºá€¸á€…á€•á€ºá€¡á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€•á€¼á€¯á€á€²á€· Intelligent Power Network á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  

> â€œA Smart Grid is an intelligent electricity network that integrates advanced communication, automation, and renewable energy to deliver reliable, efficient, and sustainable power.â€

---

## **1. Concept of Smart Grid**

Traditional Power Grid á€Ÿá€¬ One-way flow á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  
Power station á€™á€¾ â†’ Transmission â†’ Distribution â†’ Consumersá‹

**Smart Grid** á€™á€¾á€¬á€á€±á€¬á€· Two-way communication á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

ğŸ” Power & Information Flow â†’ Bidirectional  
Consumers can also become **Prosumers** (Producers + Consumers).

---

## **2. Key Features of Smart Grid**

| Feature | Description |
|-----------|----------------|
| **Bidirectional Communication** | Data exchange between user and utility |
| **Real-time Monitoring** | Sensors and IoT devices track voltage, current, frequency |
| **Automation** | Self-healing and automatic fault detection |
| **Demand Response** | Adjusts load according to supply conditions |
| **Integration of Renewables** | Solar, Wind connected efficiently |
| **Decentralized Generation** | Microgrids, distributed power systems |

---

## **3. Architecture of Smart Grid**

**Main Components:**

1. **Smart Power Generation**  
   - Renewable sources (Solar PV, Wind, Hydro)  
   - Microturbines and fuel cells  
   - Real-time load balancing

2. **Smart Transmission**  
   - HVDC and FACTS for long-distance, high-capacity transmission  
   - Digital protection and self-healing lines  

3. **Smart Distribution**  
   - Distribution Automation (DA)  
   - Smart sensors and fault locators  
   - Real-time reconfiguration

4. **Smart Consumers**  
   - Smart Meters, Smart Appliances  
   - Demand-side management  

5. **Communication Network**  
   - Fiber optics, PLC (Power Line Communication), and Wireless systems  

---

## **4. Smart Meters and AMI (Advanced Metering Infrastructure)**

**Smart Meter** á€á€Šá€º  
Electricity usage á€€á€­á€¯ real-time á€á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€¸á€á€¬á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€•á€¼á€®á€¸  
Two-way communication á€–á€¼á€„á€·á€º Utility Company á€€á€­á€¯ á€•á€¼á€”á€ºá€•á€±á€¸á€”á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

**Functions:**
- Real-time billing  
- Remote disconnection/reconnection  
- Time-of-Use (TOU) pricing  
- Data analytics  

**AMI Components:**
- Smart Meter  
- Communication Network  
- Meter Data Management System (MDMS)

---

## **5. Internet of Things (IoT) in Smart Grid**

> IoT enables real-time sensing, monitoring, and control of the power network.

**Applications:**
- Smart transformers  
- Remote substation monitoring  
- Predictive maintenance  
- Asset tracking  
- Consumer-level automation (smart plugs, thermostats)

**Benefits:**
- Enhanced reliability  
- Reduced downtime  
- Data-driven decision-making  

---

## **6. Role of Artificial Intelligence (AI) and Machine Learning**

> AI helps in optimizing grid performance, forecasting, and fault management.

**Applications:**
- Load forecasting  
- Fault detection & isolation  
- Renewable power prediction  
- Energy theft detection  
- Predictive maintenance  

**Techniques Used:**
- Neural Networks  
- Fuzzy Logic  
- Reinforcement Learning  

---

## **7. Integration of Renewable Energy**

**Renewables in Smart Grid:**
- Solar PV farms  
- Wind turbines  
- Biomass and Hydro  
- Energy storage systems

**Challenges:**
- Intermittency (variable generation)  
- Grid stability  
- Power quality

**Solutions:**
- Real-time monitoring via IoT  
- Smart Inverters  
- Energy Storage and Microgrids  

---

## **8. Distributed Generation (DG)**

> DG means power generation at or near the point of use.

**Examples:**
- Rooftop solar  
- Small wind turbines  
- Fuel cells  
- Combined Heat and Power (CHP) units  

**Advantages:**
- Reduced transmission losses  
- Improved reliability  
- Supports rural electrification  

---

## **9. Microgrids**

> A Microgrid is a localized grid that can operate independently or connected to the main grid.

**Components:**
- Distributed Energy Resources (DERs)  
- Energy Storage Systems (ESS)  
- Control Systems  
- Smart Loads  

**Operating Modes:**
- **Grid-connected mode**  
- **Islanded mode** (stand-alone operation)

**Use Case:**  
Military bases, remote villages, hospitals, data centers.

---

## **10. Energy Storage Systems (ESS)**

> ESS balances generation and demand in real time.

**Types:**
| Type | Example | Application |
|---------|--------------|----------------|
| **Battery Storage** | Li-ion, Na-ion | Solar, EVs |
| **Mechanical** | Flywheel | Frequency stabilization |
| **Thermal** | Molten salt | Concentrated solar |
| **Pumped Hydro** | Reservoir-based | Large-scale storage |

**Benefits:**
- Stabilize renewable energy  
- Backup power  
- Peak shaving and load leveling  

---

## **11. Demand Side Management (DSM)**

> DSM is the modification of consumer load patterns to balance supply and demand.

**Methods:**
- Load shifting (use power during off-peak hours)  
- Peak shaving  
- Smart pricing (Time-of-Use rates)  
- Automated Demand Response (ADR)

**Advantages:**
- Reduces system stress  
- Optimizes generation  
- Lowers cost to consumers  

---

## **12. FACTS and HVDC in Smart Grid**

**FACTS (Flexible AC Transmission Systems):**  
Enhance controllability and stability of AC grids.

| Device | Function |
|-----------|---------------|
| **STATCOM** | Voltage support |
| **SVC** | Reactive power compensation |
| **UPFC** | Full control of voltage and phase |

**HVDC (High Voltage DC Transmission):**  
Efficient long-distance, cross-border transmission.  
Used for renewable integration and interconnections (e.g., Indiaâ€“Myanmar HVDC project).

---

## **13. Smart Substations**

> Intelligent substations with digital sensors, automated switching, and data communication.

**Functions:**
- SCADA integration  
- Fault isolation and self-healing  
- Condition monitoring  
- Digital relays and sensors  

---

## **14. SCADA and Energy Management System (EMS)**

**SCADA (Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition):**
- Remote monitoring and control  
- Real-time visualization of power flow  

**EMS (Energy Management System):**
- Optimal scheduling of generation  
- Load forecasting  
- Economic dispatch  

---

## **15. Cybersecurity in Smart Grids**

> As grids become digital, cybersecurity becomes essential.

**Threats:**
- Data theft  
- Unauthorized control  
- Malware attacks  

**Countermeasures:**
- Encryption and authentication  
- Network segmentation  
- AI-based anomaly detection  

---

## **16. Electric Vehicles (EVs) and Smart Charging**

> EVs are both consumers and storage units of electricity.

**V2G (Vehicle to Grid):**
- Bidirectional flow of energy between EVs and grid.  
- EV batteries help balance load during peak hours.

**Smart Charging Stations:**
- Real-time communication with grid  
- Dynamic pricing  
- Renewable energy integration  

---

## **17. Smart Grid Communication Technologies**

| Technology | Medium | Example |
|----------------|--------------|----------------|
| **PLC (Power Line Communication)** | Wired | Smart meters |
| **RF Mesh Network** | Wireless | IoT devices |
| **Fiber Optic** | High-speed | Backbone communication |
| **4G/5G** | Mobile | Remote monitoring |
| **Satellite Link** | Long distance | Remote microgrids |

---

## **18. Benefits of Smart Grids**

âœ… Improved reliability and power quality  
âœ… Efficient energy usage  
âœ… Real-time monitoring  
âœ… Renewable integration  
âœ… Lower operational costs  
âœ… Consumer empowerment  

---

## **19. Challenges in Smart Grid Implementation**

| Challenge | Description |
|----------------|----------------|
| **High Initial Cost** | Sensors, meters, communication systems |
| **Cybersecurity Risks** | Data protection and privacy |
| **Interoperability** | Integration between old and new systems |
| **Skilled Workforce** | Need for trained engineers |
| **Regulatory Issues** | Standardization and policies |

---

## **20. Future Power Systems**

> The Future Power System is a **Digital, Decentralized, and Decarbonized** network.

**Trends:**
- AI-driven grid optimization  
- Blockchain-based energy trading  
- Peer-to-peer (P2P) energy exchange  
- 100% Renewable Energy targets  
- Integrated EV and energy storage  
- Autonomous power networks  

---

## **21. Case Study: Indiaâ€“Myanmar Smart Grid Cooperation**

- India and Myanmar signed MoUs for **HVDC Interconnection** and **Smart Grid Collaboration**.  
- Objective: Renewable integration, power trade, and rural electrification.  
- Expected Capacity: 500 MW HVDC link (Imphalâ€“Tamu).  
- Timeline: Conceptual phase, under regional grid plan (SAARCâ€“BIMSTEC).

## **1. Classification of Energy Sources**

| Type | Example | Renewability |
|--------|----------------|----------------|
| **Non-Renewable** | Coal, Oil, Natural Gas | Limited, polluting |
| **Renewable** | Solar, Wind, Hydro, Biomass | Inexhaustible, clean |

---

## **2. Solar Energy**

> Solar Energy á€á€Šá€º á€”á€±á€›á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€á€¼á€Šá€ºá€™á€¾ á€œá€»á€¾á€•á€ºá€…á€…á€ºá€…á€½á€™á€ºá€¸á€¡á€„á€º á€•á€¼á€±á€¬á€„á€ºá€¸á€œá€²á€‘á€¯á€á€ºá€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸ á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹

---

### **Solar Radiation Concepts**

- **Solar Constant (S):** ~1367 W/mÂ² (outside atmosphere)
- **Insolation:** Solar energy received per unit area
- **Angle of Incidence (Î¸):** Determines absorbed power

---

### **Solar Energy Conversion Methods**

| Type | Description | Example |
|--------|----------------|----------------|
| **Solar Thermal System** | Converts sunlight â†’ heat | Water heater, solar cooker |
| **Solar Photovoltaic (PV) System** | Converts sunlight â†’ electricity | Solar panels |

---

### **(a) Solar Thermal Systems**

**Components:**
- Solar collector (Flat Plate / Parabolic)
- Heat transfer fluid
- Storage tank

**Applications:**
- Domestic hot water  
- Industrial drying  
- Power generation (CSP â€“ Concentrated Solar Power)

---

### **(b) Solar Photovoltaic (PV) Systems**

> Semiconductor-based device converts sunlight directly into electricity.

**Basic Equation:**


P = V Ã— I
Î· = (Output Power / Incident Solar Power) Ã— 100%


**PV Cell Material:** Silicon (Mono/Polycrystalline), Thin-film, Perovskite  

**Typical Efficiency:** 15â€“22%  

**Advantages:**
- No moving parts  
- Modular and scalable  
- Works in remote areas  

**Limitations:**
- Intermittent (depends on sun)  
- High initial cost  
- Energy storage required  

---

## **3. Wind Energy**

> Converts **kinetic energy of air** into mechanical or electrical energy using a **Wind Turbine**.

---

### **Basic Principle**

**Power in wind:**


P = Â½ Ã— Ï Ã— A Ã— vÂ³

Where  
Ï = air density (kg/mÂ³),  
A = swept area,  
v = wind speed.

**Maximum extractable (Betz Limit):** 59.3%

---

### **Wind Turbine Components**

- Rotor blades  
- Gearbox  
- Generator (Synchronous or Induction)  
- Tower  
- Yaw system (orientation)  

---

### **Types of Wind Turbines**

| Type | Axis | Use |
|--------|-----------|-----------|
| **Horizontal Axis** | Parallel to ground | Most common |
| **Vertical Axis (Darrieus, Savonius)** | Perpendicular | Simple, low power |

---

### **Advantages:**
- Free fuel (wind)  
- Low operational cost  
- Clean and sustainable  

**Disadvantages:**
- Intermittent  
- Noise and visual impact  
- Requires suitable location  

---

## **4. Hydroelectric Power**

> Converts **potential energy of stored water** into mechanical and then electrical energy.

---

### **Working Principle**

Water from high reservoir â†’ Turbine â†’ Generator â†’ Power output



P = Ï Ã— g Ã— Q Ã— H Ã— Î·

Where  
Ï = water density,  
Q = flow rate,  
H = head,  
Î· = efficiency.

---

### **Types of Hydro Plants**

| Type | Head | Capacity | Example |
|---------|----------|---------------|---------------|
| **High Head** | >300 m | Pelton wheel | Mountain region |
| **Medium Head** | 30â€“300 m | Francis turbine | River systems |
| **Low Head** | <30 m | Kaplan turbine | Run-of-river |

---

### **Advantages:**
- Renewable, reliable  
- Quick start-up  
- Long life span  

**Disadvantages:**
- Environmental impact (ecosystem, displacement)  
- High capital cost  

---

## **5. Biomass Energy**

> Biomass is organic material (plants, wood, waste) converted into energy.

---

### **Conversion Processes**

| Process | Product | Example |
|-------------|----------------|----------------|
| **Combustion** | Heat, steam | Biomass boiler |
| **Gasification** | Producer gas | Bio-gas plants |
| **Fermentation** | Alcohol (Ethanol) | Biofuel |
| **Anaerobic Digestion** | Methane gas | Sewage treatment |

---

### **Advantages:**
- Carbon neutral (COâ‚‚ absorbed by plants)  
- Waste utilization  
- Suitable for rural areas  

**Disadvantages:**
- Land use competition  
- Lower efficiency  
- Pollution if poorly managed  

---

## **6. Geothermal Energy**

> Energy derived from **heat inside the Earthâ€™s crust**.

---

### **Working Principle**

Hot water or steam from deep wells drives turbines.

**Temperature:** 200â€“500Â°C at 3â€“5 km depth

**System Types:**
- Dry steam
- Flash steam
- Binary cycle (heat exchanger)

---

### **Applications:**
- Power generation  
- District heating  
- Greenhouse agriculture  
- Industrial processes  

**Advantages:**
- Continuous base-load energy  
- Low emissions  
- Compact plant area  

**Disadvantages:**
- Limited geographic availability  
- High drilling cost  

---

## **7. Ocean Energy**

> Uses ocean tides, waves, and temperature differences.

| Type | Principle | Example |
|--------|----------------|----------------|
| **Tidal Energy** | Rise and fall of sea | Barrage or tidal stream |
| **Wave Energy** | Surface motion of waves | Point absorbers |
| **OTEC (Ocean Thermal Energy Conversion)** | Temp difference (surface vs deep) | Tropical areas |

---

## **8. Hybrid Renewable Systems**

> Combining two or more renewable sources to improve reliability and efficiency.

**Examples:**
- **Solar + Wind Hybrid:** Continuous generation  
- **Solar + Biomass:** For rural electrification  
- **Wind + Hydro:** Grid stabilization  

**Benefits:**
- Reduced intermittency  
- Energy storage optimization  
- Greater reliability  

---

## **9. Energy Storage in Renewable Systems**

| Storage Type | Example | Use |
|----------------|---------------|----------------|
| **Battery** | Li-ion, Flow battery | Solar/wind storage |
| **Mechanical** | Flywheel, Compressed air | Frequency control |
| **Thermal** | Molten salts | CSP plants |
| **Hydrogen** | Fuel cells | Long-term storage |

**Equation (Energy stored):**


E = Â½ C VÂ² (for capacitor-based)

# âš¡ Chapter 21 â€“ Energy Storage, Smart Grids & Future Electric Mobility  
*(Hydrogen, Batteries, Electric Vehicles, and Grid Integration)*

---

## **Overview**

**Energy Storage Systems (ESS)** á€á€Šá€º  
á€œá€»á€¾á€•á€ºá€…á€…á€ºá€…á€½á€™á€ºá€¸á€¡á€„á€º á€‘á€¯á€á€ºá€œá€¯á€•á€ºá€™á€¾á€¯á€”á€²á€· á€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€…á€½á€²á€™á€¾á€¯á€¡á€€á€¼á€¬á€¸ á€á€€á€ºá€á€™á€ºá€¸á€•á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€¸á€†á€­á€¯á€„á€ºá€›á€¬ á€™á€Šá€®á€™á€¾á€¯á€€á€­á€¯ á€–á€¼á€±á€›á€¾á€„á€ºá€¸á€•á€±á€¸á€á€²á€· á€”á€Šá€ºá€¸á€•á€Šá€¬á€–á€¼á€…á€ºá€á€šá€ºá‹  
á€¡á€‘á€°á€¸á€á€–á€¼á€„á€·á€º Renewable Energy (Solar, Wind) á€á€½á€±á€™á€¾á€¬ á€¡á€›á€±á€¸á€€á€¼á€®á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

> â€œEnergy storage and smart mobility are the twin pillars of future power systems â€” ensuring reliability, flexibility, and sustainability.â€

---

## **1. Need for Energy Storage**

**Energy generation â‰  Energy demand (time mismatch)**  
- Solar â†’ only daytime  
- Wind â†’ irregular  
- Demand â†’ 24-hour varying pattern  

**Energy Storage** á€€ á€’á€® gap á€€á€­á€¯ á€–á€¼á€±á€›á€¾á€„á€ºá€¸á€•á€±á€¸á€á€šá€ºá‹

**Main Purposes:**
- Peak load balancing  
- Grid stability  
- Emergency backup  
- Renewable integration  

---

## **2. Classification of Energy Storage Systems**

| Type | Sub-Type | Example |
|----------|-----------------|----------------|
| **Mechanical** | Pumped Hydro, Flywheel, Compressed Air | Grid storage |
| **Electrical** | Capacitor, Supercapacitor, SMES | Short-term storage |
| **Electrochemical** | Batteries (Li-ion, Lead-acid) | EVs, solar |
| **Thermal** | Molten Salt, Ice Storage | CSP, HVAC |
| **Chemical** | Hydrogen, Synthetic Fuels | Long-term storage |

---

## **3. Mechanical Storage**

### **(a) Pumped Hydro Storage (PHS)**
- Uses two water reservoirs (upper & lower).  
- During low demand â†’ pump water up.  
- During high demand â†’ release water to generate power.  

**Efficiency:** 70â€“80%  
**Applications:** Grid load leveling  

---

### **(b) Flywheel Energy Storage**
- Rotating mass stores kinetic energy.
- Quick response, high power density.



E = Â½ I Ï‰Â²


**Advantages:** Fast discharge, long life  
**Limitations:** Expensive bearings, standby losses  

---

### **(c) Compressed Air Energy Storage (CAES)**
- Air compressed and stored in underground caverns.
- Released to drive turbines.

**Efficiency:** 50â€“70%  
**Used for:** Large-scale grid support  

---

## **4. Electrochemical Storage (Batteries)**

### **Battery Basics**

> Battery stores electrical energy in chemical form and releases it through electrochemical reactions.

**Key Parameters:**
- Voltage (V)  
- Capacity (Ah)  
- Energy Density (Wh/kg)  
- Cycle Life  
- Efficiency  

---

### **Battery Types**

| Type | Energy Density | Applications | Remarks |
|-----------|----------------|----------------|----------------|
| **Lead-Acid** | Low | Backup, UPS | Cheap but heavy |
| **Nickel-Cadmium (NiCd)** | Medium | Aircraft, railways | Long life, toxic |
| **Lithium-Ion (Li-ion)** | High | EVs, laptops, solar | Lightweight, efficient |
| **Flow Battery** | Medium | Grid storage | Scalable, durable |
| **Sodium-Sulphur (NaS)** | High | Utility-scale | High temperature required |

---

### **Li-ion Battery Structure**

- **Anode:** Graphite  
- **Cathode:** LiCoOâ‚‚, LiFePOâ‚„  
- **Electrolyte:** Lithium salt (LiPFâ‚†)  
- **Separator:** Ion-conducting membrane  

**Reaction during discharge:**


LiC6 + CoO2 â†’ C6 + LiCoO2 + Energy


**Advantages:**
- High energy & power density  
- Low self-discharge  
- Fast charging  
- Recyclable  

---

## **5. Supercapacitors**

> Stores energy electrostatically (not chemically).

**Equation:**


E = Â½ C VÂ²


**Advantages:**
- Rapid charge/discharge  
- Long life (1M cycles)  
- High power output  

**Used in:** Hybrid EVs, regenerative braking, UPS backup  

---

## **6. Hydrogen Energy Storage**

> Hydrogen acts as a clean energy carrier for long-term storage.

**Production (Electrolysis):**


2Hâ‚‚O â†’ 2Hâ‚‚ + Oâ‚‚

**Storage:** Gas tanks or liquid form  
**Conversion back:** Fuel cell â†’ Electricity  

**Advantages:**
- Zero emission  
- High energy per kg  
- Long-duration storage  

**Challenges:**
- Storage difficulty  
- Infrastructure cost  

---

## **7. Fuel Cells**

> Converts chemical energy directly into electrical energy using hydrogen and oxygen.

**Reaction:**


2Hâ‚‚ + Oâ‚‚ â†’ 2Hâ‚‚O + Electricity + Heat


**Types:**
- **PEMFC (Proton Exchange Membrane)** â€“ for EVs  
- **SOFC (Solid Oxide Fuel Cell)** â€“ for industry  
- **AFC (Alkaline Fuel Cell)** â€“ aerospace  

**Efficiency:** 50â€“70%  
**Applications:** Electric vehicles, backup power  

---

## **8. Smart Energy Storage Systems**

> Integration of ESS with **IoT + AI** for predictive control.

**Features:**
- State of Charge (SoC) monitoring  
- Load forecasting  
- Peak demand optimization  
- Grid synchronization  

**Example:** AI-based battery management systems (BMS)  

---

## **9. Electric Vehicles (EVs)**

> EVs use stored electrical energy (battery or fuel cell) to power electric motors.

---

### **EV Components**

| Component | Function |
|----------------|----------------|
| **Battery Pack** | Energy storage |
| **Inverter** | Converts DC â†’ AC |
| **Motor** | Converts electric â†’ mechanical |
| **Controller** | Manages power flow |
| **Charger** | External power supply |

---

### **Types of EVs**

| Type | Description | Example |
|-----------|----------------|----------------|
| **Battery Electric Vehicle (BEV)** | Fully battery powered | Tesla Model 3 |
| **Hybrid Electric Vehicle (HEV)** | Engine + motor | Toyota Prius |
| **Plug-in Hybrid (PHEV)** | Rechargeable battery + engine | Hyundai Ioniq |
| **Fuel Cell EV (FCEV)** | Hydrogen-powered | Toyota Mirai |

### **Advantages of EVs**

âœ… Zero tailpipe emissions  
âœ… High efficiency (80â€“90%)  
âœ… Low noise & maintenance  
âœ… Regenerative braking  
âœ… Smart grid integration

âŒ Limited charging stations  
âŒ High initial cost

## **11. Vehicle-to-Grid (V2G) Technology**

> Allows bidirectional energy flow â€” EVs can both **draw and supply** power to the grid.

**Benefits:**
- Grid balancing during peak hours  
- Emergency backup supply  
- Revenue for vehicle owners  

**Equation (simplified):**


P_grid = P_load - P_EV


**Countries Implementing:** Japan, UK, Norway, India (pilot phase)

## **1. Concept of Energy Efficiency**

**Efficiency (Î·):**


Î· = (Useful Output Energy / Input Energy) Ã— 100%


**Key Idea:**  
á€¡á€‘á€½á€€á€ºá€€á€­á€¯ á€™á€œá€»á€±á€¬á€·á€˜á€² á€…á€½á€™á€ºá€¸á€¡á€„á€ºá€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€…á€½á€²á€™á€¾á€¯á€€á€­á€¯ á€œá€»á€¾á€±á€¬á€·á€á€»á€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸á‹

**Examples:**
- LED light bulbs (90% efficiency)
- High-efficiency motors
- Smart HVAC systems

---

## **2. Importance of Energy Efficiency**

âœ… á€œá€»á€¾á€•á€ºá€…á€…á€ºá€á€¯á€¶á€¸á€…á€½á€²á€™á€¾á€¯á€œá€»á€¾á€±á€¬á€·á€á€»á€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸  
âœ… á€á€˜á€¬á€á€†á€®á€¡á€„á€½á€±á€€á€¯á€”á€ºá€á€€á€ºá€á€¬á€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸  
âœ… COâ‚‚ á€‘á€¯á€á€ºá€œá€½á€¾á€„á€·á€ºá€™á€¾á€¯ á€œá€»á€¾á€±á€¬á€·á€á€»á€á€¼á€„á€ºá€¸
