# âš™ï¸ Chapter 24 â€“ Experimental Methods and Testing of Materials  
*(From â€œStrength of Materialsâ€ by G.H. Ryder, SI Units)*  

---

## **Introduction**

In engineering, the **mechanical properties of materials** must be determined accurately before use.  
Theoretical strength values are not enough â€” because real materials contain **defects, micro-cracks, and impurities**.  
Therefore, laboratory tests are conducted to measure **elastic, plastic, and failure characteristics** under different loading conditions.  

The main objectives of these tests are:  
- To determine **mechanical properties** (strength, ductility, hardness, toughness, etc.)  
- To check **quality control** and **uniformity** of materials  
- To establish **design data** for safe working stress  

---

## **Common Mechanical Tests**

### 1ï¸âƒ£ **Tensile Test (Tension Test)**

**Purpose:**  
To determine the materialâ€™s behavior under **tensile load** until fracture â€” gives **stress-strain curve**.

**Specimen:**  
Usually cylindrical or flat with standardized dimensions (e.g., 20 mm dia, 200 mm gauge length).

**Procedure:**  
- The specimen is gripped in a **Universal Testing Machine (UTM)**.  
- Axial tensile load is applied gradually until fracture.  
- Load and elongation readings are recorded continuously.

**Measured Properties:**  
- **Elastic limit**  
- **Yield stress (Ïƒ_y)**  
- **Ultimate tensile stress (Ïƒ_u)**  
- **Breaking stress (Ïƒ_b)**  
- **Percentage elongation**  
- **Reduction of area**

**Key Formulae:**  
\[
Ïƒ = \frac{P}{A}, \quad Îµ = \frac{Î´L}{L}
\]
\[
E = \frac{Ïƒ}{Îµ}
\]

**Observation:**  
Mild steel shows distinct **yield point**, ductile fracture (cup and cone),  
while brittle materials (cast iron, concrete) fail suddenly without yielding.

---

### 2ï¸âƒ£ **Compression Test**

**Purpose:**  
To determine behavior of materials under **compressive loading**.

**Specimen:**  
Usually shorter and thicker than tensile specimen (e.g., cube, cylinder).  

**Applications:**  
Used for **concrete, cast iron, and masonry** where compressive strength governs design.

**Procedure:**  
Specimen is placed in **Compression Testing Machine (CTM)**,  
load applied axially until failure.

**Results:**  
Stressâ€“strain curve is nonlinear; ductile metals bulge (barrel shape) due to **Poissonâ€™s effect**.

**Compressive stress:**
\[
Ïƒ_c = \frac{P}{A}
\]

---

### 3ï¸âƒ£ **Hardness Test**

**Purpose:**  
To measure the **resistance to indentation** â€” indicates **surface strength** and **wear resistance**.

**Common Methods:**

| Test | Principle | Indenter | Measurement |
|------|------------|-----------|--------------|
| **Brinell** | Impression of steel ball under load | 10 mm steel ball | Brinell Hardness Number (BHN) |
| **Vickers** | Diamond pyramid under load | Diamond pyramid | Vickers Hardness Number (VHN) |
| **Rockwell** | Depth of penetration | Steel or diamond cone | Rockwell Hardness Number (HRB, HRC) |

**Typical formula (Brinell):**
\[
BHN = \frac{2P}{Ï€D(D - \sqrt{D^2 - d^2})}
\]

---

### 4ï¸âƒ£ **Impact Test**

**Purpose:**  
To measure the **toughness** of material â€” its ability to absorb energy during **sudden impact**.

**Types:**
- **Charpy Test** â†’ specimen supported as beam, struck at center.  
- **Izod Test** â†’ specimen clamped vertically as cantilever, struck at free end.

**Result:**  
Impact energy (in Joules) = energy absorbed before fracture.

**Observation:**  
- Ductile materials â†’ high impact energy (large plastic deformation).  
- Brittle materials â†’ low impact energy (sudden fracture).

---

### 5ï¸âƒ£ **Fatigue Test**

**Purpose:**  
To study material behavior under **repeated cyclic loading** â€” important for rotating shafts, aircraft wings, bridges, etc.

**Principle:**  
A specimen is subjected to alternating stress (tensionâ€“compression or bending)  
until failure occurs.

**Result Curve:**  
**Sâ€“N Curve** (Stress vs. Number of cycles)

**Key terms:**
- **Endurance limit (Ïƒ_e):** maximum stress that can be repeated indefinitely without failure.  
- **Fatigue life (N):** number of cycles to failure at a given stress.

---

### 6ï¸âƒ£ **Creep Test**

**Purpose:**  
To determine **time-dependent deformation** of materials under constant load and temperature â€” especially in turbines, boilers, or jet engines.

**Procedure:**  
Specimen loaded at **high temperature (0.3â€“0.6 Tâ‚˜)**,  
elongation measured over time.

**Creep curve:**  
Has three regions:
1. **Primary creep** â€“ decreasing rate  
2. **Secondary creep** â€“ steady rate  
3. **Tertiary creep** â€“ accelerated rate leading to rupture  

**Creep rate (ÎµÌ‡):**
\[
ÎµÌ‡ = \frac{dÎµ}{dt}
\]

---

## **Testing Machines and Instruments**

| Equipment | Function |
|------------|-----------|
| **Universal Testing Machine (UTM)** | Tension, compression, bending tests |
| **Torsion Testing Machine** | Shear modulus and torsional strength |
| **Hardness Tester** | Surface strength |
| **Impact Testing Machine** | Charpy and Izod tests |
| **Fatigue Testing Machine** | Cyclic loading endurance |
| **Creep Testing Machine** | High temperature deformation |

---

**Typical Tensile Test Curve (Mild Steel):**

(Origin)


---

## **Material Property Summary**

| Property | Determined by | Indicates |
|-----------|----------------|-----------|
| Elasticity | Tensile test | Ability to return to original shape |
| Plasticity | Tension/Compression | Permanent deformation |
| Ductility | Tensile/Impact | Elongation before fracture |
| Toughness | Impact test | Energy absorbed before fracture |
| Hardness | Indentation test | Resistance to wear |
| Fatigue strength | Fatigue test | Resistance to cyclic stress |
| Creep resistance | Creep test | Resistance to deformation over time |

---

## **Practical Importance**

- Ensures **material reliability** before use in structures, machines, and transport.  
- Prevents **sudden catastrophic failure**.  
- Helps engineers design for **factor of safety (FOS)** based on real behavior.  
- Provides **standard data** for international codes (e.g., ASTM, ISO, BIS).  

---

## **Key Takeaways**

- Every engineering material must be **tested** before application.  
- Different tests simulate different **types of loading** (static, dynamic, cyclic, thermal).  
- Data obtained define **stressâ€“strain relationships**, crucial for design and analysis.  
- Testing bridges the gap between **theory and real-life performance**.  

---

> â€œA materialâ€™s true character reveals itself not in its formula,  
> but in how it withstands the test.â€  
> â€” *G.H. Ryder*
